Northwest Frontier Inspection Diary (1) Feng Youzhen 72

Xi'an Newsletter: Luo Junren, Minister of Foreign Affairs and Minister of Judicial Administration, was ordered by the central government to inspect Xinjiang. He departed from Beijing at 8:00 am on August 25th on a special Air Eurasia No. 1 plane. I, the reporter, was invited to accompany him, and I was extremely fortunate. This trip will take three or four months through three or four provinces. Through Mr. Luo's inspection, the political and diplomatic situation of the border provinces, as well as the customs and habits of the people, can be thoroughly understood, and estrangement can be eliminated. The next day, he will report to the central government to strengthen the border defense and eliminate worries about the west. This trip is truly magnificent. I, the reporter, am grateful for the rare opportunity of this trip and for the government's special treatment of me. Therefore, I will record what I have seen and heard on this trip and share it with the people of the country.

(1) Saying Goodbye Carefully 73

August 25th, the weather was clear, but the sun was scorching, unlike early autumn. We thought that the climate would be colder when flying in the air, so we all changed into jackets in the morning, which caused us to sweat profusely and was unbearable. The new No. 1 plane prepared by Air Eurasia arrived in Beijing from Shanghai at about 6:00 am. We then took a car to Ming Palace Airport at about 7:00 am. When we arrived, hundreds of people, including central figures, officials from both the Ministry of Justice and Foreign affairs, and colleagues from the news media, had come to say goodbye. Their high affection and deep friendship were deeply felt. The No. 1 plane has a load capacity of 600 kilograms. Before the departure, it is necessary to weigh it as usual. We first went to the office to complete the procedures. After weighing the results, our luggage was simple, only 410 kilograms. Returning to the airport, the President of the Executive Yuan, Wang, also came by car to send off Minister Luo. It was 8 o'clock when it was time to leave. We shook hands with the send-off people one by one to say goodbye, and boarded the plane together. With a word of farewell, the plane quickly took off into the air. We said goodbye to Kyoto temporarily and began our journey of thousands of miles.

(2) Misfortune in the Plane 74

This is the first time I have traveled by plane, and I did not expect a big joke to happen just three minutes after taking off. Because I suffer from myopia, friends advised me to prepare an extra pair of glasses to prevent accidents in the remote border areas. So, three days before the trip, I got a new pair of glasses, which were quite suitable in terms of light and style. I was very happy and proud of myself. Unexpectedly, just three minutes after the plane took off, I felt phlegm stuck in my throat and wanted to spit it out. As soon as I leaned my head out of the window, I felt dizzy. I quickly touched my face with my hand, and my newly fitted glasses were gone. They had been blown away by the hurricane in the air. I felt lost for a long time.

(III) Another Layer of Heaven 75

After setting off for about ten-odd minutes, we encountered heavy fog. We felt a slight bumpiness and unevenness. The pilot then adjusted the plane upwards, piercing through the clouds and fog. In an instant, we had ascended to seven or eight thousand feet. At this altitude, the sky seemed boundless. The plane was also calm and steady. However, looking down, layer upon layer of white clouds rushed by like flowing arrows. Sunlight streamed down through the gaps in the clouds, casting mottled dark shadows on the earth. The rivers and roads crisscrossed like threads. Trees and houses were faintly discernible. After flying for two hours, the white clouds became even denser, sometimes rising and falling like lofty mountains and towering ridges, sometimes stretching endlessly like snow-covered plains. I thought I would only be able to witness such spectacular scenery upon reaching the north and south of the Tianshan Mountains. I never expected to have an unobstructed view of it just after leaving the capital. At this moment, the earth was completely separated from us. What people on the ground see as the sky is what we see as the earth, and we are in yet another layer of heaven. The plane flew smoothly without any discomfort, only the deafening noise was annoying, and the climate was quite cold, my lined clothing insufficient to withstand it, for we were already at an altitude of over ten thousand feet. Around twelve o'clock, the clouds parted and the fog dissipated. The plane descended slightly. Looking down, we saw layers upon layers of green mountains, densely overlapping, with sharply cut peaks and steep cliffs, presenting a perilous scene. We knew we were flying over the famous mountains of West Yue. Chang'an was in sight. It had only been five hours since we left Beijing. I could hardly believe we had traveled a thousand one hundred li.

(IV) Safely Arrived in Xijing 76

At one thirty, we arrived and landed at the airfield outside Xi'an City. Xi'an time was twelve forty-five in the afternoon, a difference of forty-five minutes from Nanjing time. Due to the plane's tire rupture, we stopped in the west corner of the airfield. Reception personnel immediately sent a car to greet us. Chairman Shao Liyu of the Shaanxi Provincial Government, along with the provincial government committee members and department heads, and Director Yang Hucheng of the Xi'an Pacification Commissioner's Office, along with various section chiefs, led the entire Special Task Force soldiers to be on guard and welcome us at the airfield. Minister Luo then, amidst the resounding music, accompanied Shao, Yang, and others as they rode into the city and settled down at the Xincheng Building. The Xincheng refers to the earthen city built by Feng Huanzhang when he was stationed in Shaanxi in the fifteenth year of the Republic (1926), specifically for training soldiers. The building is the residence built by Feng, now the residence of Yang, who diligently trains soldiers as in the past. Yang specially offered the building to Minister Luo, a hospitality that is greatly appreciated. After resting briefly at the residence, we had lunch, during which we discussed the matter of relocating convicts to build roads. Shao, Yang, and others all expressed their support in principle, but the scale is grand, and detailed measures are still under discussion. After the meal, Minister Luo, accompanied by Meng Yidong, President of the Shaanxi Provincial High Court, led me to inspect courts at all levels.

(V) Inspecting the Courts 77

Around two o'clock, we first arrived at the High Court. President Meng, Chief Prosecutor Zhang Luxian, and the presiding judges of each court received us in the president's office for a discussion. President Meng earnestly detailed the judicial situation and difficulties in Shaanxi Province, with many pertinent points. The biggest difficulty for the Shaanxi judiciary is the shortage of funds. As a result, not only are the facilities crude and simple, but the salaries of judges are also meager, to the point where they cannot even afford to feed and clothe themselves, especially in the North and West circuits.

Prince Carl of Sweden (marked with an X) photographed during his visit to the Imperial Tombs in Beijing.

(International Photographic News Agency)

Judges are almost considered a path to be feared. President Meng has only been in Shaanxi for three months, and has a good relationship with the local government. Under the previous Chairman Yang Hucheng, he was able to increase funding by a quarter. The current Chairman Shao is also doing his best to maintain it, but it's a drop in the bucket and ultimately of no help. Minister Luo, after hearing this, deeply felt that the current judicial system needs significant improvement, especially in terms of funding. The principle of inter-provincial fiscal support should be adopted, and a comprehensive plan should be drawn up. Because our country is vast, and the wealth and poverty of each province are uneven, the situations are different. If we have uniform treatment, then legal professionals will be reluctant to go to poor provinces. Talent will be concentrated in rich areas, competing for positions, and engaging in mutual sabotage. If we want the legal world to be clear and pure, it will be impossible. Minister Luo then instructed President Meng to report the economic situation of the Shaanxi judiciary in detail to the Ministry, in order to compile the situations of each province and have the Ministry deliberate and come up with a regulatory plan after reorganizing the national legal system. This will prevent the hardship of no one being willing to come to the border provinces and the talent shortage from worsening, while preventing the concentration of talent in transportation areas and encouraging competition and sabotage. The so-called judicial funding should include the following points: (1) the treatment of judges, (2) the shortage of office expenses, (3) the amount of provincial funds that are insufficient, (4) a detailed comparison of the cost of living in Shaanxi and Nanjing, (5) other special circumstances. After the discussion, we inspected the various departments within the court. The court staff, despite their economic difficulties, were able to work diligently, which is commendable. Around three o'clock, we went to inspect the First Prison. Chairman Shao was already there, so we went together to observe the actual situation in the prison. The facilities of the First Prison are simple, and the prison cells are dilapidated. The walls are made of earth, and the windows are small. This is unavoidable due to limited funds. Fortunately, the outdoor open-air corridor is large enough for the prisoners to absorb sunlight and breathe fresh air, so many of those with disheveled hair and dirty faces are still strong and healthy. Minister Luo asked many questions about the reasons for the prisoners' crimes. Generally, male prisoners are mostly convicted of assault, and female prisoners are mostly convicted of murder. This is probably due to the strong and tough nature of the people in the north. The prison is not very crowded. Minister Luo instructed that the system of suspended sentences and bail should be actively implemented when the opportunity arises. Then we visited the prison workshop, which is also inadequately equipped due to lack of funds, so only a small number of prisoners are working. However, the products, such as wooden tables, wooden chairs, and cotton fabrics, are still of considerable quality. After the inspection, we went to the Chang'an District Court and the detention center with Chairman Shao. Minister Luo personally inquired about the detention dates of those being detained in the detention center. If some were not legal, he immediately ordered that the litigation be expedited and not be delayed, so as not to increase the suffering of the people. Around six o'clock, we returned to Xincheng. Shao and Yang jointly hosted a banquet, with military and political authorities in attendance. We parted after enjoying ourselves. Then I telegraphed Dean Wang and Chairman Zhu in Lanzhou to report on the itinerary, and scheduled to fly to Lanzhou at ten o'clock tomorrow morning.

(VI) Rain Hinders Travelers 78

On the 26th, I woke up early in the morning. Looking out the window, I saw the sky overcast with continuous drizzle. The pilot called, saying that the route was full of high mountains, and the climate was not suitable for flying, so the departure had to be postponed for a day. The Northwest has suffered from drought for many years, and the people are suffering greatly. This welcome rain is naturally pleasing to them. It is said that the wheat harvest every year depends entirely on the autumn rain. If the autumn rain is suitable, then next year's wheat harvest will be abundant. Spring rain is less important. Therefore, although our departure is delayed by a day, when I think of the abundant harvest next year and the disaster relief, I rejoice for tens of millions of disaster victims in the Northwest. Around eight o'clock, Minister Luo returned the visit to Chairman Yang, Wang and Shao. Then, accompanied by Chairman Shao, we visited the Beilin (Stele Forest). The Beilin is a famous historical site in Xi'an, built in the Tang Dynasty. It has a rich collection of famous steles and pagodas from various dynasties, numbering more than four hundred. The most popular inscriptions, such as the Xuanmi Pagoda, the Duobao Pagoda, the Controversy over Seats, Wang Youjun's Daya Collection, and the Thirteen Classics, are all erected here, making people linger and reluctant to leave. Around ten o'clock, we went to the Provincial First Library to visit this place's collection of famous and valuable carvings, utensils, books, and paintings from past dynasties, which is quite rich. The most notable is the Song Dynasty Qisha Tripitaka, with more than seven thousand volumes, secretly stored in a room with special protection. I heard that Shanghai bookstores have already issued printed versions for sale, worth more than five hundred gold. In addition, there is a Tang bell hanging on a frame, about three or four feet high, from the Tang Jingyun era (710-711 AD). There is also a Zhou Dynasty bronze tripod, valued at thirty thousand yuan. Other famous and valuable items are too numerous to mention. After browsing, we returned to the residence for lunch. It continued to rain in the afternoon, so we stayed in the residence and did not go out. Around four o'clock, Yang and Shao visited successively and had a meeting with Minister Luo. At six o'clock, Meng Zhaodong, President of the High Court, and Zhang Luxian, Chief Prosecutor, hosted a banquet. We returned to the residence at half past seven. The rain was still drizzling, but the pilot called, saying that we could hope to depart for Lanzhou at eight o'clock tomorrow morning.

(VII) A Glimpse of Xi'an 79

We have only been in Xi'an for two days. It is almost impossible to talk about what we have observed in such a rush. Well, let me briefly describe my impressions based on what I have heard and seen. The Three Qin regions have been the area for building capitals throughout the dynasties, and have been repeatedly devastated. The historical sites are no longer what they were. In recent years, natural disasters and man-made disasters have followed one after another. The suffering of the people is even more unbearable. Looking up, one sees yellow sand everywhere, fully expressing the unique desolation of the Northwest. Nine out of ten houses in Xi'an City are earthen walls with tile roofs. The market is bleak and withered, so it is not difficult to imagine what the situation in the countryside is like. Fortunately, the local military and police maintain public order effectively. Recently, they have repeatedly captured major bandits, solving many problems for the people. The government is working hard on construction, but it is difficult to make progress quickly due to economic constraints. The roads in the city are wide and flat, almost comparable to those in Beijing and Shanghai. Unfortunately, except for the east and west avenues, which are gravel roads, the rest are mud roads. When it is sunny, the sand flies around; when it rains, the mud splashes everywhere. In terms of transportation, the city relies entirely on rickshaws and donkey carts. Only the government agencies have one or two cars. Now, cars are used to travel east to Tongguan and west to Lanzhou, but donkey carts are still the main mode of transportation. The currency system used to be quite chaotic, but it has gradually stabilized after reorganization. Central government banknotes are fully accepted. Provincial banknotes fluctuate every day, worth about ninety cents of a silver dollar. The newspaper industry is gradually developing. There are three or four daily newspapers, such as the Xijing Daily, the Culture Daily, and the Qin Daily, publishing either two large sheets or one large sheet each day. The Xijing Daily is the most common. There are also three or four news agencies, such as the Xi'an branch of the Central News Agency and the Border Affairs News Agency. The Central News Agency branch is the most important. In the future, it is necessary to actively develop this to communicate news from the Northwest. Writing to this point, the reporter deeply feels that Shaanxi is an important town in the Northwest, with a vast area and sparse population, and abundant resources. It is urgent to actively develop it. Speaking of development, the following two points are particularly urgent: (A) Develop water conservancy. The reason why Shaanxi Province has suffered so terribly from disasters in recent years is because water conservancy has not been repaired, leading to drought and famine, and thousands of miles of red land. Although Shaanxi has the Yellow River and the Jing and Wei rivers, the area covered by the rivers is limited. Recently, although the Jingwei Canal has been built, irrigation only reaches three or four counties because the branch canals have not been completed. It is said that the rivers in the counties of northern Shaanxi are of no use to agriculture and rely entirely on the weather. Therefore, developing water conservancy is extremely urgent. On the one hand, dredge the rivers; on the other hand, complete the branch canals. Secondly, afforestation can regulate the climate and is also very important. Recently, I heard that the Agricultural and Forestry College has found a site in Wugong and will start operating within the year. Its future benefits will certainly be significant. (B) Develop transportation. Throughout Shaanxi Province, except for the area from Xi'an east to Tongguan and west to Lanzhou, where cars can pass, the rest of the transportation is extremely congested. Shaanxi is rich in products, such as coal and cotton, but they are difficult to transport and inconvenient to export. Therefore, developing transportation is extremely urgent, especially completing the Longhai Railway. This is not only beneficial to boosting commerce and immigrating to open up the border, but also has significant implications for military and political affairs. Recently, the American wheat loan has been concluded, but the use and distribution have not yet been determined. If the central government plans the overall situation and pays attention to the Northwest, using a portion for development, then the benefits

Page 12

will be significant. Furthermore, technical cooperation from the League of Nations should focus on the Northwest. Secondly, outstanding domestic talent should also penetrate into remote provinces and divide up the development, so that everything can be revived and construction can be discussed. (Sent from Xi'an on August 26)

Military Situation in Northern Fujian Intensifies Again 80

= Fiercest fighting at Xiamou and Nankou =

= Newspaper news must be inspected =

Fuzhou correspondent: Recently, the Red Bandits in Liancheng and Changting counties have been severely suppressed by the Western Fujian army. They suffered heavy losses in the Pengkou and Sibao areas and found it difficult to gain a foothold. They fled north, invading Qingliu and Mingxi. As a result, it was widely rumored in the provincial capital that Jiangle and Shunchang counties had been attacked by the Red Bandits. At present, merchants transporting goods from Fuzhou to the upper reaches have also stopped. The provincial government immediately telegraphed Wang Jicheng, Chief of Staff of the 56th Division stationed in Yanping, to inquire about the actual situation. Last night, they received Wang's reply, stating that the bandit forces in Jiangle had not succeeded, and the bandit situation in Shunchang had not changed. After dispatching a team to increase defenses in Yanping, the area was very consolidated. It can be seen that the outside rumors are untrue. Furthermore, according to front-line news obtained by a certain military agency, the 78th Division's Qu Shounian unit has now been ordered to move from Yong'an to Anxi to replace the 61st Division's Mao Weisou unit. The newly formed 2nd Division's Lu Xingbang unit, the two brigades of Lu Xingrong and Tong Yonghan, are fighting with the bandits in Xiamou, at the junction of Shaxian and Mingxi. The 56th Division's Liu Heding and Gui Zhenyuan, and Jiang Yan's two brigades, are fighting with bandits in Nankou, at the junction of Jiangle and Mingxi. The fighting is very fierce. Currently, the Liu and Lu divisions are adopting an interior line warfare tactic, luring the bandits deep and then encircling and annihilating them. The county chiefs of the nearby bandit areas did not know this and made a fuss, using alarmist language to telegraph the province for assistance. The Pacification Headquarters believed that such actions would disturb the people, and yesterday specially ordered the county chiefs to remain calm and not disturb each other, affecting public order. At the same time, the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau also stated that at this time of intense bandit suppression, newspapers should be cautious in publishing news. It specially joined the Pacification Headquarters and the Provincial Party Headquarters to establish a news inspection office, which is scheduled to start inspecting on August 29. All news from various newspapers that has not been reviewed, stamped, and sealed by the office may not be published. (August 28)

Tai, Jia, and Bao Counties Request Exemption from Winter Grain Transport Surcharge 81

= The government's extension of the levy breaks faith with the people =

= The rural economy has collapsed and it is difficult to collect the levy =

Tai, Jia, and Bao counties telegraphed the Provincial Government, requesting exemption from the winter grain transport surcharge. The text read: "Since the province of Jiangsu has been collecting a winter grain transport surcharge of two yuan per shi (unit of dry measure) since the 18th year of the Republic (1929), the people have suffered greatly from the burden of this extra tax. The people have repeatedly appealed, exhausted and hoarse, and the Ministry of Finance has taken into consideration the concerns of rural bankruptcy and telegraphed your government to collect it at half price, but it was not approved. This year, when the land price tax is collected, it is heard that this special levy must still be collected. The people are terrified upon hearing this news. We dare to analyze the reasons why the collection should be stopped for your government: Since the 17th year of the Republic (1928), the collection of the two-yuan surcharge has continued. Your government once stated that it would last for one year only and then stop. Since then, year after year, it has been extended indefinitely. There is no greater breach of faith by the government to the people. If the people have no faith, they cannot stand. If the country has no faith, how can it stand? If we want to promote the implementation of government orders, we must maintain the government's prestige. This is the first reason why it should be stopped. The rural economy is on the verge of collapse. The reason for this is the low price of rice and the heavy taxes. Those who care about the people's suffering cry out loudly and seek collective relief. But the additional levies of the warlord era are still being followed, and the cutting is endless. The people are the foundation of the country. If the foundation is strong, the country will be stable. If the people's hearts are scattered, the country will collapse. This is the second reason why it should be stopped. Since the flood in the 20th year of the Republic (1931), the counties of Jiangsu have accumulated arrears of land tax. What is collected is only about 50% or 60% of the scheduled amount. This is not because the people do not know how to serve the public, but because the heavy taxes have caused hardship. We must reduce the current burden in order to hope for the repayment of old debts. If we add extra heavy levies, it is adding difficulty to difficulty, and extra levies will not be hoped for to improve. How can special levies be scraped together? The provincial government only has a name for increasing revenue, but in reality, it is implicitly short. The national treasury and the people's livelihood both suffer. This is the third reason why it should be stopped. Tai, Jia, and Bao counties suffered from Japanese aggression last year. Nine out of ten people are destitute. The severity of the disaster is unmatched by the counties of Jiangsu Province. The two-yuan surcharge in the 21st year of the Republic (1932) was caused by the general case of the entire province. The people have repeatedly appealed, but your government has not taken this into consideration. Disaster-stricken counties are treated the same as non-disaster-stricken counties. Considering the matter, it feels very unfair. The disaster victims who have not yet caught their breath can hardly bear this extra burden. This is the fourth reason why it should be stopped. For this reason, we jointly telegraph this petition, imploring your government to permanently abolish the special levy of two yuan for the winter grain transport, starting from this year, to show great faith and relieve the people's plight. We are extremely anxious and await your orders, Tang Wenzhi, Huang Shizuo, Wang Chengxiu, Gu Rui, Qian Shitong, Gu Heshushi, Wu Shiyong, Zhao Dingkui, Qian Songpan, Pan Changyu, Chen Zuiong, Jin Chengyong, Gu Gongliang, Jiang Enjian, Gong Baolin, and others respectfully bow thirty times."

He Jian Telegraphs that Chen Wo's Troops Have Collapsed 82

= Chen's Chief of Staff Captured and Executed =

= He Sends Li Jue to Handle the Aftermath =

Changsha correspondent: Chen Wo, who stubbornly resisted in Zhijiang, is the son of Chen Hanzhang, the former commander of the 8th Independent Brigade. Chen Hanzhang was assassinated in April of the 19th year of the Republic (1930). He Jian reorganized his troops and, considering that Chen's troops were all from the upper reaches of western Hunan, Chen Wo was still in command. The brigade was incorporated into Tao Guang's division, and Chen Wo was appointed brigade commander. Later, it was disbanded again for some reason. In May of this year, Chen suddenly occupied Zhijiang, Qianyang, and Huangxian counties, appointing county chiefs and intercepting taxes. He Jian then ordered the 3rd Division's Chen Zixian and the 62nd Division's Li Guojun's two brigades to attack Chen, successively recovering Qianyang and Huangxian counties. Chen then occupied the Zhijiang County seat. He Jian ordered his troops to besiege it for more than a month, and it was finally completely recovered on August 25. Chen Wo fled alone, and his troops surrendered their weapons. He Jian immediately ordered Li Jue, the acting security commander, to go to Zhijiang to handle the aftermath. Li went on the 29th and will convene the seven county chiefs, security regiment leaders, and gentry of Qianyang, Zhijiang, Huangxian, Suining, Jingxian, and Tongdao to discuss reorganizing the local defense and handling the aftermath. Here are the telegrams from Li, Chen, and others, recorded as follows: "The rebel Chen caused chaos in western Hunan. Since our army besieged him, he relied on the lives and property of the entire city as his shield, stubbornly resisting based on the danger. It has been two months. In recent days, he has suffered too much damage, and his internal affairs have been disorganized. On the day before yesterday, our Eastern city wall blew up a cavern, injuring many bandits, which increased panic. The next morning, the Tang camp of the bandit troops guarding the outside of the South Gate surrendered their weapons to us. The bandit troops in the city burned the civilian houses along the South Gate and the Leather Street, which was a terrible sight. The officials took the opportunity to supervise the troops, surrounding the city and launching a fierce attack. The Xie camp of the Li regiment defending the East Gate and the various troops at the Water East Gate were the first to ascend the city. Chen's regiment and He's regiment then attacked from the South Gate. Chen Wo, knowing that he could not succeed, led more than two hundred bandits to rush out from the back of the West Gate. Our army struck them in the middle of the night. Only twenty or thirty people escaped. The rest either drowned or surrendered and were captured. It is said that the rebel Chen himself, his life or death is unknown. Whether he drowned is not known. In total, except for more than thirty firearms that the bandit troops escaped with, all the remaining weapons were surrendered and captured. A bandit chief of staff, Han Cihou, was captured on the spot. Rebel Chen's rebellion harmed the people, all due to his plans. The people hated him to the bone and pleaded for him to be executed on the spot to satisfy the people's hearts. As for the twenty or thirty people who escaped, we have dispatched teams to follow and chase them down, and ordered all the militia teams to encircle and suppress them along the way, in order to cut off the roots. We respectfully telegraph this report. Li Guojun, Chen Zixian, Zhou Zhaojun, and Huang Suhe kowtow, grateful."

He Jian's telegram announcing the handling of the aftermath said, "Previously, the rebel Chen Wo took advantage of our bandit suppression that was being promoted to call himself a soldier in Zhijiang and Qianzhou, disrupting the rear. The crime is unpardonable. We sent Brigade Commander Li Guojun and Brigade Commander Chen Zixian to lead troops to arrest and suppress him, and also telegraphed for assistance in the arrest. Unexpectedly, after the bandit Chen was defeated in Qianyang, he occupied the Zhijiang County seat, stubbornly resisting on the basis of the danger. This commander-in-chief sympathized with the fact that the soldiers and civilians were mixed in the city and could not bear to use intense artillery fire, resulting in the destruction of everything. Therefore, the siege lasted for more than a month. It was only on the Shen hour of that day that, relying on the bravery of our soldiers, they took the lead in climbing the city. Most of the rebel troops surrendered their weapons, and the rebel Chen Wo fled alone, swimming through the water. He is being pursued and arrested. In addition to sending Li, the acting security commander, Jue, to Zhicheng immediately, on the one hand, investigate and identify the officers and soldiers who contributed and reward them, and on the other hand, comfort and ask the people who have suffered, and find ways to resettle them and properly plan the aftermath in order to eradicate the source of the chaos. Special telegraph to notify you. Furthermore, when Chen Wo started the rebellion, Chen Changyou, the commander of the Second Regiment of Bandit Suppression in the upper reaches of western Hunan, was killed because he refused to join the rebellion. His loyalty and righteousness are admirable and deeply regrettable. Order the acting commander Li to search for the remains, properly encoffinate and bury them, and provide a generous memorial service to comfort his loyal soul. Please also be informed." (August 31)

Suzhou 83

Two Bandit Leaders Executed by Firing Squad

Lei Xiaoheizi (age 19) and Li Sanmazi (age 28), bandit leaders from Henan, colluded with other bandits to kidnap more than 20 people in Changtiangang Township in Wujiang County, including a child surnamed Zhang, a monk from Donglin Temple, and male and female hostages, a female hostage from Beifang Township, and Pan Shoucheng and his daughter Pan Aizhen from Kuilianggang Dong Township in Damiaogang, among others. Among them, those who were killed after being kidnapped accounted for five or six people. They also intercepted the Jiaxing Xinhua and Dongshan steamships, robbing more than 20 water police escort firearms. After being captured by the Wujiang County Government, they were bound to the outside of the East Gate on the morning of September 2 at 8:00 AM to be executed by firing squad.

Wuxi 84

Dispute Over the National Goods Exhibition

Qian Zhongliang, the district chief of the First District Office, believing that this year is the National Goods Year, initiated the Autumn National Goods Exhibition in order to promote national goods. He submitted it to the 42nd District Affairs Conference for discussion and decided to organize a preparatory committee, recommending nine preparatory members, and in accordance with previous precedents, the venue was still set in the city park. When it was being actively prepared, the Park Management Committee, affiliated to the City Funds Property Committee, suddenly held a meeting and decided to refuse to lend the park. Some citizens, such as Guo Jie of the Third Class, sent letters to the Park Management Committee, asking them to refuse to lend the park. However, some citizens, such as Chen Hongjun, Wu Baoquan, Zhou Yinbo, and Xue Mingjian, sent letters to the First District Office, the City Funds Property Committee, and the Park Management Committee, arguing that the exhibition should be held in the park. If the exhibition is held in a place that citizens do not pay attention to, or in a secluded place, it will be difficult to achieve the practical effect of promoting national goods. The reasons stated in their original letter are very reasonable, and they hope that enthusiastic comrades will adopt them.

Shouchang 85

Hurricane Overturns Police Boat

The 13th Team of the Chang'an Public Security Police, was ordered by the Three District Chief Shen Weiying to be led by Captain Yang Qingjiu to rush to Dahu to encircle and suppress bandits. On the 3rd, they reorganized their team to return to defense. Eight patrol boats were towed by a gasoline boat, passing through the Sujia Weng area. The river surface there was vast, and there was also a strong wind. The cable of the last boat suddenly broke, and the entire boat capsized. Wu, the squad leader, jumped out of the window into the water. The remaining team members were all overturned into the river. Fortunately, they were good at swimming and were able to swim ashore, avoiding drowning. All the equipment, firearms, and cannons on the boat were also salvaged. The only losses were ammunition and sundries, worth about 200 silver dollars.

Yangzhou 86

The Water Level of the Huai and Pi Sections of the Canal Rises Sharply Again

The Jiangbei Canal Works Bureau is working hard on flood control. Special Secretary Zhi Ying and Radio Station Director Wu Guoshi are responsible for the back-and-forth telegraphs of the water level rise and fall. They continue to work as usual even on Sundays. Yesterday (the 2nd), the bureau received a telegram from the Guide Committee, stating that there were 33 breaches in Hebei Province, each three or four li wide. It will be quite difficult to block them. If the Long surge flies and flows into northern Jiangsu, it would be a great concern. Unexpectedly, on the 3rd, a telegram was received from the Huai and Pi sections, reporting that the water level had risen again. The Yao Wan Bamboo Dam rose sharply by one foot and seven inches, the Bulao River rose one foot and four inches, and the Shuangjin Gate rose three inches. In addition, the Qingjiang Zheng Gate had a reserve of two zhang (Chinese unit of length) one foot and eight inches, and the Touba Dam had a reserve of four zhang three feet and one inch. According to a telegram from the Gao Bao section, the water level at Yumatou was seven feet and one inch. Given this water level trend, the future will be even more critical.

Military and Police Encircle and Suppress Bandits in Luyang Lake 87

Zhu Xin, a section chief of the Inspectorate Brigade, because bandits were rampant in Luyang Lake, specially transferred two platoons of 16 police officers and detectives from the investigation team to depart from the city at 10:00 PM on the afternoon of the 2nd and rushed to search and suppress the bandits. It was also heard that because the Commissioner's Office received a telegram reporting that a large number of bandits had been discovered in the Baziqiao area, in addition to rifles, pistols, box cannons, and broadswords, they also carried several machine guns. He especially ordered the team leader to lead Li's troops to rush there and join forces with the two provincial defense armies and the land and water corps police of Gao Bao and other counties to encircle and suppress the bandits from all sides to secure the local area.

Nantong 88

The Truth Behind the Female Student's Suicide by Drowning Remains Unclear

Regarding the female student who committed suicide by drowning herself from the Da Yu Steamer, it has now been learned that she was Fan Xiu, a student in the third class of the Nantong Women's Normal School. Zhang Shuzhen was her alias, and she was from Fujian. She came to Shanghai this time because she received a telegram stating that her father was seriously ill and planned to return to Fujian by sea. The reason for her suicide is unclear. The man suspected of being with her was Mao Mengjue. His uncle, Mao Maoyou, is the section chief of the Eighteenth Army's wounded soldier factory in Nantong. According to Mao, his nephew went to Shanghai to seek employment. It is also heard that Fan Xiu has an elder sister, Fan Qiong, who is studying at the Shanghai Wu Ben Girls' School.

In Hai Fu Town, located at the border of Nantong and Haimen counties, a large group of salt smugglers have gathered. The Fourth Tax Police Division has dispatched a team to suppress them.

Two Children Struck by Lightning 90

In Yan Zao, a village in the eastern part of Tongyi, during a heavy thunderstorm on the second day of the month, a boy surnamed Zhang, Zhang Bing, and his niece were sheltering from the rain in a shed near the fields when a bolt of lightning struck, killing both children. At the same time, four other children were so frightened that they became mentally deranged.

Danyang 91

Kidnapping Case in Western District Solved

Zang Xufu, a resident of Zangjia Village in the western district, and Chen Zhenggen, a young child from Zhouxiang Village, were kidnapped by bandits some days ago, who demanded a large ransom, as previously reported. It is now learned that the hostages were hidden in Bai Gushanling, Zhenjiang. The detective team of the Provincial Public Security Bureau solved the case and arrested the main bandit, Ye Jinshan, and three others on the spot. Subsequently, a suspect named Sun Yiya was also apprehended. The hostages were taken out and sent to the Provincial Security Office for punishment. After hearing the news, Magistrate Guo of this county immediately sent police to Zhenjiang to escort the bandits back to Danyang for investigation and trial.

Huzhou 92

Chief Writer of "New Huzhou" Newspaper Arrested

Zhang Jiying, the chief writer of the "New Huzhou" newspaper, is from Puyuan, 21 years old. He previously worked for the "Huzhou Newspaper" and "Huzhou Public Newspaper". In March of this year, he raised capital to prepare for the "New Huzhou" newspaper. Less than a month after its publication, at 9 a.m. yesterday, bailiffs and detectives from the Shanghai Special District Court came to Huzhou and, together with police officers from the Wuxing Local Court, arrested Zhang Jiying. He is temporarily detained in the court's detention center. This morning, he was escorted to Shanghai by the original detectives.

Hangzhou 93

Female Performer at the Great World Commits Suicide

Zhang Gendi, a female performer at the Hangzhou Great World amusement park, was 19 years old. She was unmarried and had been performing tightrope walking at the Great World for six months. Last night (the 3rd), she performed as usual. Due to a moment of carelessness, she lost her footing and fell. Her uncle, Zhang Baolin, who was directing her performance in the park, thought she had lost face and scolded Gendi after the show. Overcome with remorse, Gendi developed a pessimistic view of life and, at around 2 a.m. this morning, took advantage of the absence of others to secretly go to the river under Longxiang Bridge and commit suicide by drowning. Police officers from the local police station rushed to rescue her after being alerted, but she was already in a critical condition. She was rushed to the Municipal Hospital, but it was too late to save her. She died shortly after, which is truly tragic.

Rescuing the Baoshan Seawall 97

Provincial Technicians Expected to Arrive Today

County Government Goes to Province to Receive Funds for Urgent Repair

Two Organizations Request Allocation of Funds for Repair

The Dabaike News Agency reports that the Baoshan seawall has been damaged in ten places due to the impact of the hurricane, and the situation is extremely critical. Fortunately, the wind has subsided yesterday, avoiding further collapse. The Baoshan County Government sent two telegrams to the provincial government the day before yesterday, reporting the emergency. The provincial government has assigned technician Zhang Junsheng to go to Baoshan to inspect the damage, and he is expected to arrive today. Jin Qingzhang, the Magistrate of Baoshan County, convened an emergency meeting yesterday with various agencies, organizations, and local gentry to discuss prevention methods. They decided that the affected areas were too large and it was difficult to meet the emergency without a large sum of money. Therefore, they decided to send the County Magistrate and the Chief Technical Officer, Wan Kaijia, to the province yesterday to report to the provincial government and the Construction Department and to request funds from the Finance Department for urgent repairs. The county government is recruiting local workers to stack sandbags and stones to protect the areas that have already been damaged. Fortunately, last night was the full moon, and the moonlight was very bright, so rescue efforts continued throughout the night. Magistrate Jin Qingzhang also led Secretary Bao Siren on a personal inspection along the seawall, strictly supervising the work.

The Xinsheng News Agency reports that the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Local Coordination Association sent a telegram to the Jiangsu Provincial Government yesterday regarding the critical situation of the Baoshan seawall project, requesting the allocation of funds for repairs. The original telegram is recorded below: "To the Honorable Gu, Chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government in Zhenjiang: Regarding the request of our association and others for the allocation of funds for the repair of the Baoshan seawall, we have received your government's approval No. 1. After reading it carefully, we still have many concerns. The dangerous situation of the seawall project was previously reported by Yuan Xilian, a citizen of the county, who submitted detailed maps of the county government to your government for review. At that time, the requested amount was 200,000, while the amount re-estimated by your government's personnel was 40,000, a significant difference. This is undoubtedly a figure that cannot be saved. Blocking water is like blocking bandits, and it is difficult to estimate from afar. We believe that the number estimated by the dispatched personnel should be the basis for handling matters, as it is more practical. We are aware that the provincial treasury of Jiangsu is strained, and your government's allocation of 20,000 is undoubtedly a result of careful management. This matter concerns the lives of people in several counties. If an accident occurs, the remission of land taxes and the collection of relief funds must be carefully considered and weighed. In recent years, floods have frequently occurred in various provinces, partly because of the reluctance to spend money beforehand and the failure to prepare sufficient materials to repair each section early, leading to the sudden outbreak of disasters. The lessons of the past are not far away, and we should prevent a repeat of the same mistakes. Therefore, we dare to offer our humble opinion and humbly request your government to adopt it, which would be greatly appreciated. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Shanghai Local Coordination Association."

Also, the old soil embankment in the southern part of the southern end has collapsed with a length of about five Zhang and a width of more than five Chi. Among the above sections, Wangjiamatou and Wangjiazhai are the most dangerous. We should report this to the Honorable Magistrate for review and quickly dispatch personnel to inspect the site. In addition to supervising the patrolmen of each section to inspect the entire seawall for any danger, we will submit another report later. Respectfully reported by Zhu Huanong, Seawall Patrolman of Taicang County." Furthermore, according to yesterday's report, Wangjiazhai, north of Jiepai, was again damaged by about 20 Zhang yesterday. Kong Xiangxi Flew to Jiangxi Yesterday Morning 102

=To Attend the Lushan Conference, Will Return to Shanghai in a Few Days=

=To Discuss Methods of Economic Cooperation with Various Countries=

Kong Xiangxi, the President of the Central Bank, flew from Hongqiao Airport to Xun in a Sikorsky aircraft yesterday morning at 10:30 a.m., upon the invitation of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Military Commission and Minister Song (Ziwen) of Finance, to attend the Lushan Conference and discuss important issues such as domestic and foreign affairs and the distribution of American cotton and wheat loans. Mr. Kong is scheduled to stay in Lushan for a few days before returning to Shanghai first. Details are as follows:

Sikorsky Aircraft Flies to Xun and Transfers to Lushan 103

Mr. Kong went to the Central Bank at around 9 a.m. yesterday to handle important official matters. He returned to his private residence on West Aizaisi Road at 10 a.m., rested briefly, and then drove to Hongqiao Airport in two cars with Song Zian and his three sons and daughters. At 10:30 a.m., he boarded the Sikorsky aircraft provided by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, circled the airport once, and flew west from Shanghai. In addition to Song Zian, two attendants accompanied Mr. Kong to Lushan. Xie Linfu, the Secretary of the Central Bank, and many of Mr. Kong's sons and daughters went to the airport to see him off. Mr. Kong decided to stop briefly in Nanjing to eat before continuing his flight and is expected to arrive in Xun and climb the mountain in the evening.

Lushan Conference to Hear Reports from Cai (Finance) and Song 104

When the reporter met Mr. Kong at Hongqiao Airport this morning and asked about the focus of discussion at the Lushan Conference, Mr. Kong said that the Lushan Conference would first hear a report from Minister Song of Finance on his attendance at the Washington Talks and the World Economic Conference, as well as his inspection of various European and American countries, the recent economic situation of various countries in the world, in order to learn from the strengths of various countries and improve our country's shortcomings, and to determine the methods of economic cooperation with various countries in the world.

National Plans Depend on This 105

Mr. Kong continued, saying that the most important task for our country at present is construction, and replenishment is also an urgent matter. However, all of these require funds. Therefore, the discussion at the Lushan Conference will focus on the opening of new financial sources and the reduction of expenses. As for the American cotton and wheat loans, it has been decided that they will be used entirely for construction. However, how to allocate them will have to be decided by the Lushan Conference. This is a trivial issue and not an important topic of the Lushan Conference.

President Wang and Others Will Go to Lushan Soon 106

Mr. Kong concluded by saying that the Lushan Conference is expected to last for about five or six days. He plans to return to Shanghai first after staying in Lushan for a few days because of his busy official duties in Shanghai. President Wang (Jingwei) and the heads of various ministries will go to Lushan after the Executive Yuan meeting. Huang Yingbai, the Chairman of the Executive Yuan's Political Affairs Reorganization Committee stationed in Beiping, will also go to Lushan to participate. However, he did not hear when he would depart.

Key Participants to Discuss Various Cases 107

The names of the key central figures who have already arrived in Jiangxi or are on their way to participate in the Lushan Conference are listed below: Chairman Chiang Kai-shek (Jieshi) of the Military Commission, President Wang (Jingwei) of the Executive Yuan, President Sun (Ke) of the Legislative Yuan, Minister Song (Ziwen) of Finance, President Kong (Xiangxi) of the Central Bank, Minister Chen (Shaokuan) of the Navy, Envoy Jiang (Zuobin) to Japan, Vice Minister Tang (Youren) of Foreign Affairs, Mayor Wu (Tiecheng) of Shanghai, Vice Minister Zeng (Zhongming) of Railways, Chairman Xu (Shiying) of the Relief Committee, Central Committee Members Wu Zhihui, Zhang Jingjiang, Li Shizeng, etc. The reporter learned from political circles this morning that the Lushan Conference is scheduled to open on the 6th of this month (tomorrow) and will not be held in a formal meeting format. The conference will last for a maximum of five days. The main cases to be discussed are: (1) Opening of new financial sources and reduction of expenses in the future (2) Diplomacy (3) Construction (4) Technical cooperation between our country and the League of Nations (5) Distribution of American cotton and wheat loans (6) Relief for the Yellow River flood, and other items.

(2) If the capital side raises objections, another general strike meeting will be held on the 16th. (4) Other issues will await the arbitration or mediation of the municipal government.

Great Losses on the Beining Railway After the Violent Japanese Invasion of China 109

Movable and Immovable Property Worth Over 300 Million Yuan

Other Losses Totaling Approximately 37.6 Million Yuan

The Xinxin News Agency reports that according to sources from the Railway Bureau, the Beining Railway was the earliest railway built in China and was well-managed and commercially developed. The newly emerging railways in the three northeastern provinces relied on the support of the railway, and were able to use its surplus funds to build Huludao and Yingkou wharves. The September 18th Incident in 1931 suddenly occurred, and the Beining Railway bore the brunt of the attack, and has suffered extensive damage from the bombings and destruction by the violent Japanese, and all previous efforts were in vain. The main and branch lines of the railway were originally 822 kilometers long. Later, with the completion of the Jinzhao and Jiutong two branch lines, it increased to 1,254 kilometers. Currently, the remaining sections within the customs are 476.68 kilometers, only about one-half of the original line. According to estimates by the Beining Railway Bureau, the total value of movable and immovable property of the main and branch lines in the sections outside the customs occupied by the violent Japanese is approximately over 300 million. Other losses, after investigation

Sikorsky Aircraft Returned to Shanghai Yesterday 110

Successful Test Flight to the Philippines

In order to prepare for direct air service between China and the United States, the China National Aviation Corporation has opened a line from Shanghai to Manila in the Philippines. On the 14th of last month, Mr. Biggs-Spears, the American director of the company, along with the pilot and three other people, departed from Shanghai in a Sikorsky aircraft for a test flight and to inspect the landing field and liaise with the Philippine government. It has now been completed and returned to Shanghai at 4:20 p.m. yesterday. Details are as follows:

Details of the Test Flight 111

Mr. Biggs-Spears, the American director of the China National Aviation Corporation, accompanied by pilot Grover, co-pilot and radio operator H. Aymore, and Mr. Melner, the representative of United Airlines, departed from the Jiangmian near Longhua Airport at 5:15 a.m. on the 14th of last month and arrived safely in Hong Kong at 4:15 p.m. After staying for two days, they continued their departure from Hong Kong at 5:20 a.m. on the 16th and arrived in Manila at 3:10 p.m. They stayed there for sixteen days, continuing to explore nearby routes and discussing airport issues. On the 3rd of this month, they departed from Cavite Naval Air Station in the Philippines at 6:00 a.m., arrived in Hong Kong at 1:15 p.m., stayed in Hong Kong overnight, and took off from Hong Kong at 6:05 a.m. yesterday morning. At 7:30 a.m. they passed Shantou, at 10:45 a.m. they arrived in Fuzhou, and after refueling, they left Fuzhou at 12:00 p.m. and continued along the coast of Fujian and Zhejiang. At 4:20 p.m. they returned to Longhua Airport. The China-Philippines test flight was declared a success.

Situation Upon Arrival in Shanghai 112

After the Sikorsky aircraft took off from Hong Kong at 6:05 a.m. yesterday, it reported the situation along the way by radio. Therefore, the China National Aviation Corporation and the China Flying Transport Corporation received reports and sent personnel to Longhua Airport to welcome them. When the Sikorsky aircraft arrived at the airport at 4:30 p.m., it circled the airport twice and then gradually descended from the air and landed at the airport. Mr. Biggs-Spears and the other three jumped out of the aircraft one after another and shook hands with the welcomers, looking very happy. They then took cars to their residences to rest. The Sikorsky aircraft was pushed into the hangar by airport workers and properly secured.

Chance Encounter on the Way Back 113

Yesterday morning, when the Sikorsky aircraft was returning 200 miles northeast of Hong Kong, it happened to encounter the President Hoover, a ship of the Dollar Steamship Lines, at sea. The aircraft threw down a roll of Hong Kong newspapers to the President Hoover for the passengers to read. After receiving the report, the shipowner replied by radio to express their gratitude, saying that the presented mail would be framed and hung as a souvenir of the friendly relations between the aircraft and the ship, and wished a safe journey. After receiving the telegram, the aircraft also replied by radio, briefly stating that they were very grateful for the importance attached to the souvenirs. If this route is successful after this test flight, there will be many opportunities to meet in the future. Although the whistle of your ship was not heard, the white smoke was seen, and we are very grateful for your kindness. This is indeed a very interesting chance encounter in the successful China-Philippines test flight.

Surveying the Airport 114

According to a spokesperson of the company speaking to the Xinxin News Agency reporter, when Mr. Biggs-Spears and others arrived in Manila, they were warmly welcomed by all circles there. The Philippine government is also very enthusiastic about this and will grant United Airlines special operating rights for the Manila-Hong Kong route. Mr. Biggs-Spears has also surveyed five sites, Fuzhou, Hong Kong, Dongsha Island, Lake Prue, and Santiago Island, as airports.

Opening of the Air Service Still Pending 115

It is heard that Mr. Biggs-Spears, the American director of the company, plans to submit a detailed report to the company within a few days on the situation of the test flight from Shanghai. He also plans to prepare a comprehensive plan for opening a weekly mail flight between Shanghai and Manila and will send it to the American headquarters for decision after the business develops. Therefore, the official opening date of the Shanghai-Philippines air service has not yet been determined.

According to the accurate numbers, the total is approximately 37,600,000 yuan. The magnitude of the loss is shocking. The following is a loss survey table: (1) Loss of life of employees: 17 dead, 49 injured, and 1 kidnapped; (2) Loss of employee property: 304,176.49 yuan; (3) Loss of damaged railway property: 426,874.35 yuan; (4) Losses from looting: 1,815,437.645 yuan; (5) Loss of special expenses: 477,827.03 yuan; (6) Loss of mandatory expenses: 132,763.00 yuan; (7) Uneconomical consumption: 46,196.50 yuan; (8) Operating losses: 8,884,453.63 yuan (9) Loss of credit: 8,494,977.90 yuan; (10) Loss of life of passengers: 25 dead, 40 injured; (11) Loss of passenger property: 285,110.00 yuan, totaling 42 dead, 89 injured, 1 kidnapped, and losses of 37,588,455.35 yuan.

Italian Congressman Gori Hua Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 116

To Investigate the Production and Marketing of Raw Silk in China

Trade Bureau and Others Scheduled to Host a Banquet Tomorrow

Italy is the richest country in the production of artificial silk. It has sent Congressman and President of the Silk Industry Association Dr. Gori Hua to various countries to investigate the production and marketing of raw silk and artificial silk. It is learned that Mr. Gori Hua has completed his investigations in the United States and Japan and arrived in Shanghai at 4:30 p.m. yesterday aboard the British mail ship Awa Maru, which docked at buoy No. 13 in the Huangpu River. Those who went to the port to welcome him included Mr. Tie Langji, President of the Italian Chamber of Commerce, and representatives from the Italian Consulate in Shanghai. On the Chinese side, there were Ji Zejin and Zhang Pansun, representatives of the International Trade Bureau, and Guo Limao and Miao Zhongling, directors of the Technical Department of the Commodity Inspection Bureau. After landing, Mr. Gori Hua took a car to the Cathay Hotel to rest. He is scheduled to visit He Bingxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau, at 10 a.m. today and Cai Wuji, Director of the Commodity Inspection Bureau, at 11 a.m. It is also heard that the International Trade Bureau, the Commodity Inspection Bureau, and others are scheduled to host a welcome banquet tomorrow, which will invite the Italian Chargé d'Affaires in China, the Consul, the Counselor in Shanghai, Mr. Tang Linan, the manager of Yixing Company, and leaders from the Shanghai Raw Silk Association and the raw silk industry to accompany them. According to Ji Zejin, Director of the Guidance Department of the Trade Bureau, speaking to a reporter from the Xinxin News Agency, Mr. Gori Hua plans to stay in Shanghai for a longer period of time in order to meet with relevant parties and conduct investigations. As for whether he will go to Beijing or other ports, Mr. Gori Hua has not indicated.

The Northeastern Righteous Army is a Force to be Reckoned With 117

Many Puppet Soldiers Defecting

Japanese Supervision is Strict

The Central News Agency reports that the situation in the Northeast under the iron heel of the Japanese has been reported yesterday. The following is a compilation of the current situation of the anti-Japanese resistance, selected from the report dispatched from the Northeast by the special envoy of Mr. Cheng Yun, Commander-in-Chief of the Northeastern People's Salvation Army, on July 30, which has only recently arrived:

Bitter Resistance 118

Dating back to March 2, our Eighth Route Army, led by Zhao Zaitian, engaged in the fiercest battle with the Japanese and puppet railway guards in Shenjiazhan and Zhangjiawobao on the Huhuai Railway. The battle lasted for four days. The enemy's reinforcements arrived and surrounded our army from all sides. Our army fought hand-to-hand and broke through the encirclement, retreating to the counties of Mudan, Dongxing, and Tonghe. In this battle, 19 Japanese soldiers were killed and 12 were wounded. More than 20 puppet soldiers were killed and more than 30 were wounded. Our army lost a battalion commander, 124 soldiers were killed in action, 259 were wounded, and 351 large and small firearms were lost. On March 15, our Ninth Army, led by Ma Zhiqing, and the Xu Brigade, engaged the Japanese and puppet mixed army of Chen Decai in Dongliaodianzi Lanhou Hill, Acheng. They fought each other for a day and a night, killing 5 enemies. Our army lost 16 soldiers killed in action. Because it was too close to the transportation routes, it was not convenient to stay for a long time, so they retreated to the mountains and valleys of Nianziguo Tumenzizi. On March 27, our Tenth Army, led by Jiang Yunwu, and the Geng and Jiang brigades, attacked Bayan County in Heilongjiang, but failed. They retreated to Dongxing. On April 11, our Fourth Army, led by Song Yongzi, and the Han Brigade, engaged in fierce battles with the rebellious Yin Regiment stationed in Fuyu for three days and nights. Finally, due to the exhaustion of ammunition and the increasing urgency of the enemy's attack, they had no choice but to retreat, with one part retreating to Wuchang and another part remaining hidden in the county. In this battle, our regimental commander Bi Zhong was killed in action, and 28 soldiers were killed or wounded. More than 30 large and small firearms were lost.

Desertion of Puppet Troops 119

A contingent of puppet troops deserted, consisting of over two thousand members of the Zhu Jiachangzi militia, located in the boundary of the Third District of Changchun County. They refused to surrender their arms to the Japanese army, expressed their opposition to the Japanese, and are now located within the territory of Panshi County. Furthermore, the Thirteenth Regiment stationed at Yongji Gangyao also defected due to conflicts with the Japanese army. Additionally, a newly emerged "Steel Squad" in Yanshou County, numbering approximately 20,000, is demonstrating formidable power, having expelled Zhang Tongce, the stationed puppet army commander, from the county. Reports regarding the current location and strength of our volunteer army are withheld due to military secrecy.

Deployment of Japanese Troops 120

Concerning the deployment of Japanese troops and their deceitful tactics, the following can be stated: a large portion has been dispatched to areas along the borders of Manzhouli and Suifenhe to defend against our army. Other units are stationed at the Great Wall and Jehol. The exact number of troops stationed in each province is unknown, but they frequently issue clothing to overseas merchants. During periods of subdued news, they order troops to disguise themselves as merchants; during periods of escalating tensions, they parade through various locations to demonstrate strength. The Japanese are skilled in deceit and falsehood, and this is one example. The Japanese military depot is located in Toutaogou, the puppet capital. Its ammunition and supplies can support the troops stationed in the Northeast for three to four months. Other locations such as Liaoning, Jilin, and Harbin have insufficient ammunition and supplies, only enough to maintain the current situation.

Japanese Surveillance of Puppet Troops 121

The Japanese surveillance of the puppet troops is extremely strict, and their methods are particularly noteworthy. Recently, another troop reduction conference was held in the puppet capital, implementing reductions in troop size and reorganizations. Many Japanese personnel were incorporated. Puppet army officers holding slightly important positions are assigned a Japanese woman to secretly monitor their actions to prevent unexpected incidents. This strict surveillance is not only applied to puppet army officers but also thoroughly to lower-ranking officers. In each puppet army brigade, two Japanese regimental officers are stationed. In each regiment, two Japanese battalion commanders are stationed. In each battalion, two Japanese company commanders are stationed. If this continues, the positions of puppet army officers will likely be undermined. In reality, none of the puppet army officers genuinely support the rebels. They are merely compelled by circumstances and dare not hastily engage in desertion. Although there are some who willingly fawn over the Japanese, they are in the extreme minority, limited to those holding the highest military authority, such as the traitors Zhang Jinghui, Zhang Haipeng, and Yu Zhishan.

Page 14

The Xinming Steamer Encounters a Hurricane, Escapes Danger, and Arrives in Shanghai 122

=Encountered danger in the waters off Sheshan, both anchors broken=

=Drifted for more than twenty hours, believing it would sink=

=Four crew members injured, cargo and other items damaged extensively=

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xinming steamer, the first-class vessel in the Northern Seas route, encountered a sudden hurricane off Sheshan this time. After drifting in the sea for twenty-two hours in extreme danger, it managed to escape and arrive in Shanghai, which was truly fortunate. It now requires repairs. The details of the encounter are described below.

Hurricane Encountered at Sheshan 123

The Xinming steamer departed from Weihaiwei at 10:30 PM on August 31st. Initially, the journey was smooth and uneventful. However, at 12:00 AM on September 2nd, the steamer encountered a strong wind and showers approximately sixteen nautical miles north of Sheshan. By 1:00 PM, it received a warning from the observatory stating that a hurricane was approaching. At that time, the steamer was directly in the eye of the storm. The captain urgently wanted to return to Weihaiwei to take shelter from the wind, but it was impossible to sail north against the northeast wind. Sailing south was also impossible due to numerous reefs. The decision was made to head north, drop anchor temporarily in the heavy wind and rain, and wait for an opportunity to proceed. However, as the steamer turned, the hurricane struck. Waves crashed down like mountains overturning the sea, striking head-on and subjecting the Xinming to unprecedented danger.

Turbulent Waves Filled the Sky 124

The size of the wind and waves at that time was the largest the steamer had ever encountered. A wave crashed down, engulfing the entire vessel. Captain Ma Jiajun urgently issued an emergency mobilization order to all staff and crew, instructing them to position the ship against the wind and waves. However, the wind force was like a mountain, pushing the ship backward. They urgently dropped both anchors to try to stop the ship, but to no avail. The captain then ordered the engineers to engage full speed ahead after dropping anchor to resist the storm. However, this not only failed to make any progress but also resulted in the ship being pushed back by the waves. At this point, the entire crew was extremely anxious, as they were bound to hit a reef and break apart, causing all the passengers and cargo to be lost. This situation persisted for approximately six hours as the ship continued to be pushed backward by the huge waves. The captain then ordered more anchor chain to be released, throwing thirty fathoms of the heavy chain into the sea. Still, it was difficult to avert the crisis.

Cargo Destroyed 125

By 8:00 PM, the wind and waves intensified. A wave crashed down, sweeping away the objects on the bridge, the cargo loaded on the deck, and the passengers' luggage and trunks into the sea. The captain and chief mate were unable to work on the bridge and moved to the lower level to use a spare compass, continuing to command forcefully in the heavy wind and rain. Unexpectedly, several large waves, four or five zhang high, struck, completely destroying the grand dining room, officers' cabins, steerage cabins, the deck, railings, doors, window panels, awnings, and mooring lines. Seawater rushed into the cabins, flooding the entire ship. The ship suddenly pitched and rolled, making it impossible for people to stand. Over three hundred crew members and passengers were submerged in water.

Chain Breaks, Anchor Lost 126

At this critical moment, wireless messages were frequently sent, but the Xujiahui station's antenna was broken, and communication was impossible. Over two hundred passengers on board scrambled to the grand dining room, crying and wailing in despair. Employees of the business department also knelt in the water, praying to the gods. The captain ordered the engagement of the fastest speed, hoping to withstand the onslaught. At approximately 3:00 AM on the third day, they saw the anchor chain spark and heard a loud crash. Both chains had broken, and both massive anchors had been lost at sea. The ship suddenly tilted, threatening to capsize in the sea. At that moment, the captain believed that he would not survive and tried to pull out his pistol to commit suicide but was disarmed by the chief mate. Just as the situation was most critical, a huge wave arrived and righted the Xinming, which was a stroke of great fortune. Otherwise, the entire ship would have been destroyed.

Drifting on the Sea 127

After the chains broke, Captain Ma ordered the remaining heavy chain on board to be released into the sea, abandoning any hope of survival. He then used a sounding line to measure the depth. At 4:00 AM on the third day, the depth was measured at five fathoms (thirty feet). The crew was even more terrified, as the ship was approaching the beach and reefs. The ship had lost control, and if it continued to drift backward, it would shatter on the reefs and no one would survive. Just as they were preparing to distribute life jackets to the passengers, they suddenly received a report from the observatory stating that the wind direction had shifted from northeast to northwest. Examining the barometer on board, they saw it gradually rising. A glimmer of hope appeared as they narrowly escaped death. They redoubled their efforts to push forward. From the start of the storm to the shift in wind direction, the Xinming had drifted on the sea for a total of twenty-two hours.

Escaping from Death 128

At 5:00 AM on the third day, the wind and waves were still strong, and the showers continued. Fortunately, the direction had shifted, and the Xinming was drifting further out to sea, escaping the danger of the beaches and reefs. At that time, the ship was still drifting against the waves. By 9:00 AM after dawn, it had escaped the greatest danger, and the wind gradually subsided. The observatory reported that the hurricane was at 123 degrees east longitude and 32 degrees north latitude. Captain Ma urgently ordered the anchor to be raised, adjusted the course southward, and calculated that from the encounter with the wind to that point, the entire crew and sailors had worked hard in the storm for forty hours without sleep or food. At this time, they did not know where they were. At 12:00 PM, they gradually saw a mountain. Captain Ma checked the chart and realized that they had reached Huanao Island. It was estimated that they had drifted over forty nautical miles from Sheshan due to the wind. However, although the wind had subsided, they still could not navigate. No ships were visible on the sea. It was not until 4:00 PM that they reached Daji Island, giving everyone on board hope for survival.

Sailors Injured 129

According to Captain Ma, who spoke to reporters, this was the first time he had encountered such a storm. He believed there was no hope of returning alive, but the fortunate escape was due to both human effort and divine assistance. The reporter was shown the damaged cabins, almost none of the doors and windows were intact. At the most dangerous time, the water depth on the upper deck was three to four feet, indicating the extent of the flooding in the other cabins. Four sailors and helmsmen working on the deck were struck by a large wave that swept from the bow to the stern. The four were thrown against the iron fixtures on the deck, each suffering serious injuries. One helmsman was even more severely injured. Other crew members and sailors suffered minor injuries from being struck by the waves. Objects inside the cabins were either swept away or washed into the sea, resulting in significant losses.

Arrived in Port Yesterday Morning 130

The Xinming managed to escape danger and set sail for Shanghai at 1:00 PM on the third day. It was not until 6:30 PM that the ship reached the mouth of the Yangtze River outside Wusong. At that time, because the anchors had been lost, they had to retreat and anchor outside Songkou. They were only able to enter port yesterday morning and arrive at the Jinliyuan Wharf. By then, the passenger accommodations and deck structures had been badly damaged. A report was immediately made to the general office, and Liu Hongsheng dispatched engineers to inspect the ship and arrange for major repairs to prepare for reinstallation. Generous consolation was also given to the crew who had survived the ordeal. Their safe arrival in Shanghai after surviving such danger was due to the efforts and blood of the crew. The passengers on board were also overjoyed upon arrival. Although all their luggage had been lost, they admired Captain Ma's composure in the face of adversity. Everyone's life was spared, feeling as if they had been reborn. However, when they went ashore, their clothes were soaked, and they were in a state of disarray. The total loss was estimated to be at least thirty to forty thousand taels of silver.

Captain's Lingering Fears 131

Captain Ma also told reporters that when the Xinming arrived at Dongsha, the lightship there, which was supposed to guide ships, had been swept away by the storm. The lighthouse was extinguished and dark, and the lightship was nowhere to be seen. The personnel managing the lightship must have also encountered danger. Furthermore, the lights of the Yangtze River estuary lighthouse were also extinguished by the storm, causing the Xinming to grope its way in the dark. The wireless antenna at Xujiahui was also damaged by the hurricane, preventing ships at sea from communicating. It was heard that the Taikoo Swatow steamer also encountered the storm and delayed its arrival by two days, expected to arrive in Shanghai today.

Zeng Pu and Others Request Exemption from Winter Grain Transport Tax and Surcharge 132

Zeng Pu and others sent a telegram to Finance Minister Song, which read: "To Song Jun, Finance Minister of the Capital and Vice President of the Executive Yuan: Since the Jiangsu Provincial Government abolished the grain transport tax in 1930 and replaced it with a land price tax, the case of continuing to levy a surcharge of two yuan per dan of winter grain has been presented to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance, following old errors. The provincial legal bodies and citizens of various counties, based on legal facts, have repeatedly resolved not to extend the collection and have appealed for a stop. The Ministry was repeatedly requested and approved to advise the province to correct this. After the disaster, the people of Jiangsu were hoping for relief. It is recently heard that this surcharge is still listed in the provincial budget for 1933, and there is talk of seeking approval from the Ministry in advance without waiting for your return. It is reported that you have achieved great success at the World Economic Conference in obtaining silver agreements and technical cooperation. Standards for rationalizing finances have long been established. Jiangsu Province is located near the capital, making administrative compliance convenient. Surely there is no lack of methods to alleviate poverty. Yet, the province only knows to seek profit, not caring for the people's labor, and wants to reverse course and impose a surcharge in a time of long-abolished grain transport and plummeting grain prices. It seeks to extend the evil precedent by using high-pressure tactics to deceive the central government with this illegal levy. We fear that the rural economy will be increasingly on the brink of collapse. What about the reconstruction plan? This will harm your reputation and distant views, and it is not just the people of Jiangsu who will suffer deeply. We ask that you investigate and reject the proposal for Jiangsu Province to continue collecting the surcharge this year, and order that the previously collected amounts be refunded in installments under the regular tax items to maintain national credibility and care for the people's livelihood. We urgently await your orders. Respectfully submitted on behalf of the citizens of Changshu residing in Shanghai: Zeng Pu, Di Liangsun, Yu Chengmei, Zhang Lansi, Huang Bingyuan, Weng Zhilin, Weng Zhilong, and Zeng Xubai, all kowtowing in support."

Lin Wojiang reported on the preparations for the naming ceremony of the five aircraft. 2.
