The Tragic Situation in Yingfu County After the Disaster 134

As Many as Four Thousand People Torn Up

The Red Swastika Society Is Urgently Implementing Relief Measures

The Southeast Main Association and Shanghai General Office of the Red Swastika Society received a letter from Relief Commissioner Wang Daoyuan yesterday, describing the cruelty of the bandits, which brought tears to the reader's eyes. The original letter is recorded below: "Respected Sirs: I have received your telegram with reverence. The number of towns and villages in Yingfu and Taihe Counties that have been burned, looted, and kidnapped is as many as twenty-five. After pursuit and suppression, the bandits have moved from Taihe towards Zhoukou, but there are still traces of bandits in Tai territory. The cruelty of the bandits is unprecedented. Of the eight thousand people who were kidnapped, over one thousand were torn up in Nanzhao Village, and three thousand were torn up in the old county of Taihe. The number of those who were ransomed is limited, because once a hostage enters bandit territory, they are subject to multiple factions. Each faction will conduct searches, and if money is found, it is confiscated regardless of whether it is for ransom. When the money is taken, the hostages cry and plead with the faction, but they are accused of lying, and either their ears are cut off, or one of their hands is severed, and they are sent back to raise money. If the money is not delivered by the deadline, they are killed. Children of eight years old are tied together in a string, nine and ten-year-olds are tied together in another string, and those over ten are tied together in a string, all connected with hemp ropes. They are beaten with whips and forced to 'jump and run' for the bandits' amusement. Kidnapped women are forced to march naked, providing amusement at any time. However, those who are truly wealthy and have a reputation are placed on large tables, turned upside down with the legs facing up, and carried by four men using wooden poles, called 'God of Wealth.' They are even provided with food and drink at each location. If the ransom is not paid by the deadline, they will not be spared. The bandits have many cavalrymen, and their saddles are made from chairs that have been sawed in half, using two chair surfaces joined together as one saddle, allowing for rapid movement. All of this was recounted by refugees who escaped from the bandit dens. After consulting with representatives from Ying, Shang, Fuyang, and Zhengyang, we have decided to start with Nanzhao Village in Ying and Liujia Village in Fu, conducting investigations and releases as we go. We have already arrived in Ying to investigate. After finishing the investigation and release, we will proceed from Ying to Fu, and from Fu to Tai. However, the roads are difficult, requiring either soil carts or walking, making it impossible to move quickly. The most difficult thing is that the houses in the disaster area have been reduced to ruins, making food and accommodation inconvenient. We have already brought dry food and water bottles. In addition, although the corpses in various towns have been buried by the Ying and Fu associations, many have drowned in rivers and wells, making the drinking water smell foul. There are many epidemic cases among the disaster victims. Therefore, we requested in the previous telegram that more medicines be allocated for distribution to the disaster areas. The Anhui Provincial Government has also dispatched four relief commissioners, and the relief funds amount to only five thousand yuan. They are currently convening a meeting of officials and gentry to discuss solutions."

Also attached is a letter from the Yingxi Refugee Appeal Group, which reads: "To our fellow countrymen, elders, brothers, and compatriots in Anhui Province: Alas! Is there anyone in the world who has suffered a more tragic and cruel disaster than we refugees of Yingxi, who are in deep water and fire and displaced by bandits? If we were to enumerate the various cruelties we have endured, and convey them one by one to your ears, we fear that even the hearts of stone would be moved. All those who are human beings will gnash their teeth and tear their eyes. We refugees are residents of the Shahuang Two Rivers in Yingxi. In the past, we have suffered from natural and man-made disasters, which were already numerous enough. Recently, disaster has struck from the sky, and bandits have risen up, raping, killing, burning, and looting with extreme cruelty, reducing houses to ruins, wealth to ashes, and people to death. We refugees fled in panic, luckily escaping slaughter. We fled by boat to the docks of Liuzikou, Baliduo, and Yujiatan. Our frightened souls were barely settled, and our breathing had not yet returned to normal when we began to think about the ruined property, the lack of livelihood, the displacement of the population, and the inability to return home. Every time we think of this, we choke with sobs and feel desperate. But our bad luck has not ended, and it is like adding snow to frost. Some people claiming to be from the Zhengyang Boat Tax Office sent out rowboats carrying seven soldiers with guns, going to each dock to forcibly collect boat taxes and personnel registration fees, as well as fees for kerosene. We refugees have difficulty getting enough to eat, so how can we afford to pay taxes? If we object even slightly, we are immediately whipped. Those who cannot pay the tax are detained in the two water prisons, and there are almost no exceptions. Those who were unable to pay the taxes were detained in the two waterways administrations. Over the past few days, almost all who were hoisted up to show off and whipped and beaten have been released after Wang, the President of the Merchants Association, offered a guarantee of release. The other 20 people or so were released on bail for a fee. We refugees weep and think that even if the checkpoints were normally dignified, those who had to pass through would be required to declare their taxes. However, the Boat Tax Office is far away in Zhengyang and, regardless of whether we passed through or not, sees where the profit is and goes its own way. It sends boats upstream for several or even dozens of miles to force the collection of taxes, knowing only to scrape as much as possible to make a profit, regardless of the pitiful lives of the refugees. The government is sending troops to suppress the bandits, and charitable organizations are raising funds for relief, but the Boat Tax Office alone is intensifying its actions, violating the law and harming the people, treating hundreds of refugee boats as a source of profit. With such measures, the refugees will have no place to call for justice, and the accumulated resentment will be difficult to express. The resulting grievances will inevitably lead to droughts and floods. Alas, what is the point of the government sending troops to suppress the bandits? What is the point of charitable organizations raising funds for relief? We refugees have suffered cruelly and present our case with tears. We implore our fellow countrymen, elders, brothers, and compatriots to uphold justice, provide us with assistance, and fundamentally abolish this illegal and harmful Boat Tax Office to provide relief to the refugees. We respectfully make this request, and we beg you to consider."

Reports Received by the Chinese and Foreign Joint Relief Association Regarding the Yellow River Flood Disaster 135

Shandong Association in Beijing: This time, the Yellow River flood has caused a major disaster in the four provinces of Hebei, Shandong, Henan, and Jiangsu. The disaster is especially severe in the ten-odd counties of Heze, Juye, Fan, Pu, Yuncheng, Dongping, and Shouzhang in Shandong. The houses have been destroyed by the flood. The disaster victims are climbing on roofs and trees, crying for food. The old and weak are rolling in the ditches, dying. We are calling on our relatives and friends to show compassion and beg from door to door. There are no houses with fires in the neighborhood. We urgently request quick relief.

Dingtao County, Shandong: On August 13, the Yellow River breached its banks, flooding directly into the county. Over one hundred villages south of the city were turned into a vast ocean. For over ten nights, torrential rain poured down. The cries of tens of thousands of people shook the wilderness. We beg for urgent relief.

In addition to dispatching special commissioners to conduct on-site investigations, the association has also received reports from Chinese and Western personnel in the disaster areas. After the dike breach in Henan, the flood spread to dozens of counties in Hebei, western Shandong, and northern Jiangsu, drowning over a million people. There are over thirty-three breaches along the Yellow River, causing losses of over ten million yuan. The disaster victims are currently struggling in the water, crying out for help. Their lives are in danger. The association is reportedly working with Western staff in various disaster areas to find ways to provide rescue. However, as the weather is gradually turning cold and there are wails of grief everywhere, with no place to eat or sleep, if they do not become victims of the flood, they will inevitably die from the epidemic. We urgently hope that charitable people from all walks of life will show great compassion, quickly provide assistance, and perform broad-based charitable deeds. As the association does not have branches, donations can be sent directly to Room 402, No. 12 Renji Road, Shanghai.

Detailed Report of the Fuyang Disaster Received by the Jisheng Society 136

The Chinese Jisheng Society recently received a report from the Fuyang Relief Committee of Anhui, stating: "Fuyang is located on the border of Anhui, adjacent to Henan, and is traditionally an area where bandits emerge. In late July, local bandits such as Zhang Xueliang and others colluded with defeated soldiers. Regiment Commander Cheng Yaode made a major eastward move, reaching Song Village on Sunday and Yingxiandian on Monday, merging with the bandits Jiang, Ma, Fan, Ba, Yang, Xiaohei, and Zi who had captured Pochu Village. The total number of bandits was approximately eight thousand. On Tuesday, they reached Fan Village, and on Wednesday, they reached Tongzhen Village, Tianpeng Village, and Xincun Village. On the 30th, they reached Datian City Village and Cheng Village. On the 31st at night, the bandits arrived at the city and harassed it for several hours. At dawn, they circled the Five Li Temple south of the city, Nine Li Gully, Seven Li Store, Eighteen Li Store, Thirty Li Store, Forty Li Store, and Siliu Village, occupying them for three days. On Sunday, they reached Fifty Li Store and Sixty Li Store, and Xinjizi. On Monday, they reached the Ying County territory, West Sixty Li Store, Fifty Li Store, Forty Li Store, Thirty Li Store, and Da Bali Store, occupying places such as Runhe Village. On Tuesday, they occupied Nanzhao Village, and then reached Zhangjiazhai and Gaogangtou in the Third District of this county. By Wednesday, Cheng Ziyi, the commander of the Henan Security Team, led two regiments of infantry and one regiment of cavalry to Jiao Po Village and advanced along two routes. When they reached Nanzhao Village, they engaged the bandits, fighting fiercely for two days and nights. On Thursday, the bandits retreated from Sixty Li Store, circled the city, turned northwest, and occupied Datian City Village for one day. On Friday, they crossed the Quan River and occupied the old county of Taihe territory via Jia Village, Jiangjia Hall, Wen Village, and Hua Village. The killing and wounding along the way were countless, and tens of thousands of men and women were kidnapped. The east-west span was three to four hundred li, and the north-south span was over one hundred li. The people and livestock were almost all slaughtered, the village houses were burned to the ground, and corpses were everywhere, with a stench that could not be tolerated. There were severed heads, broken abdomens, amputated limbs, peeled skin, cut ears, cut breasts, nailed hearts, and nailed hands. Those near the river were driven into the water, and pregnant women were thrown to their deaths, and the infants were thrown as well. The extreme cruelty cannot be fully described, even worse than the Communist bandits. Survivors have no houses to hide their heads, no clothes to cover their bodies, and no food to fill their stomachs. If relief measures are not taken, they will still have nowhere to escape death. As the autumn coolness gradually sets in, they will inevitably perish together. Thinking of the future, we are extremely heartbroken. In addition to sending telegrams to appeal, we beg you to allocate large sums of money to save the people from the disaster. We urgently await your orders." The disastrous situation has reached this extreme. The association has no funds to provide relief and hopes that compassionate and virtuous people within the country will take this opportunity to save and bless, and the merits will be boundless. Perhaps we can save the survivors from one in ten thousand.

Sichuan Compatriot Association Fundraising for Red Zone Disaster Relief 137

The Sichuan Shanghai Compatriot Association, due to the plight of over two million refugees from the ten-plus red zones in northern Sichuan, who are displaced and wandering in eastern and western Sichuan, has previously resolved on numerous aid measures and formed a special fundraising committee. Qiu Zhizhong, Li Qingfan, Yu Yuanhui, Zheng Yutang, Li Xunfu, Shao Jigao, and Fu Yaquan were appointed as committee members. It has been learned that the association believes that fundraising will not be effective without gathering the strength of many people, so they expanded the committee membership, adding Yang Shukan, Huang Fusheng, Gu Ao, Tan Yigong, Wu Shan, Xia Lianggong, Lai Xin, Ji Jingyu, Yang Suichu, Xiong Zhefan, Xie Dekan, Huang Fugong, Song Yuqi, Liu Shouchuan, Luo Huizong, Yang Dequan, Chen Ding'an, Liu Bingyi, Kuang Bing, Zeng Yiyi, She Yuanbai, Su Yuguang, Yang Junmu, Liao Yanlun, Yang Haifeng, Ye Huasheng, Guo Menggeng, Zhang Maoxiu, Qiu Shunqing, Deng Zhiyan, Huang Yunqing, Yuan Ziqi, Peng Xiaofu, Guo Shaoyun, Xiang Xinru, Li Yunjie, Lu Jizeng, Jiang Rongsheng, Yang Bingzhi, Qu Zaizhi, Yang Junqing, Zhong Hangsu, and others as committee members. The committee was officially established yesterday at the association's office, and the following resolutions were made: (1) Zheng Yushu and Shao Jigao were elected as the chief and deputy leaders of the fundraising group; Yang Daochu and Su Yuguang were elected as the chief and deputy leaders of the collection group; Yu Yuanhui of Juxingcheng Bank was elected as the leader of the custody group; Li Qingfan and Li Xunfu were elected as the chief and deputy leaders of the administrative group; Qiu Zhizhong and Yang Junqing were elected as the chief and deputy leaders of the document group; and the leaders of each group will serve as standing committee members. (2) It was decided to host reporters from various newspapers and news agencies in the city at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA at 2:00 PM this Friday (the 8th), and to invite Liu Zizhong and other representatives from the Sichuan Northwest Red Zone Disaster Relief Petition Delegation to report on the disaster situation. (3) Prominent Sichuanese figures in Beijing, such as Shi Qingyang, Lü Chao, and Sun Yuanliang, have replied, expressing their willingness to donate funds or come to Shanghai to jointly plan the effort. A letter will be sent to Chairman Shi Qingyang, inviting him to quickly come to Shanghai with other compatriots to jointly host various charitable organizations and philanthropists in this city and request relief. (4) The administrative group will quickly prepare several fundraising books, with the introduction drafted by the document department, and all committee members listed by name. (5) Committee members who do not hold leadership positions in any group will serve as fundraising committee members in the fundraising group, with ten people forming a team to quickly solicit donations externally. (6) The collected donations will be gathered by the collection group every ten days, announced publicly, and handed over to the custody group for safekeeping. (7) All expenses of the association will be donated by the committee members themselves. All the funds raised will be used for disaster relief and will not be used for administrative expenses. (8) This special committee will be externally known as the Sichuan Shanghai Compatriot Association Relief Committee for the Red Zone Disaster in Northern Sichuan, and a seal will be printed to demonstrate credibility. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions were passed.

Young Man and Woman Commit Suicide by Jumping into the Huangpu River 143

Boarded the Da Lai Ferry and Jumped into the Water Near Pudong

The Bodies of the Man and Woman Were Recovered Separately Yesterday, No Suicide Notes Found

At 8:00 PM on the 1st of this month, a fashionable young man and woman boarded a small Da Lai Company ferry at the Hankou Road Customs Wharf, hand in hand, seemingly intending to go to the company's (McKinley) world-class giant ship "President," which was berthed between No. 10 and No. 13 of the Yangshupu Customs. At that time, the sailors on the small ferry were convinced that they were going abroad. Unexpectedly, when the ferry arrived near the Pudong cemetery pier outside Hongkou, this couple took advantage of an opportunity when no one was paying attention and suddenly jumped hand in hand into the turbulent waves. In that instant, the sailors on the ferry tried to save them, but it was too late. They stopped the engine to rescue them, but they had already sunk and disappeared. Afterwards, the ferry captain, Wang Arong, returned to the shipping company and found that the man and woman had not purchased tickets and were not passengers going abroad. They reported it to the Customs Police Station for the families to inquire. Unexpectedly, after the two people fell into the water, their bodies had already separated. At 6:00 AM yesterday, the man's body floated to the surface of the Huangpu River in Lujiazui and was recovered by Chinese police officer No. 30 from the Water Police Station. As for the woman's body, it was found floating downstream in the Yangshupu Huangpu River and was also recovered by Chinese police officer from the Water Police Station. The two bodies were not yet rotten. At 11:00 AM in the morning, when the tide was rising, the No. 2 patrol boat of the Nanshi Lifesaving Bureau transported the two bodies to the bureau one after another. The bureau's staff inspected them and found that the man was wearing a Western suit with a white Indian silk shirt, a black sports vest, yellow trousers, blue cotton shorts, a white belt, black socks, and yellow running shoes. He had long hair and was about 20 years old. He seemed to be a handsome young man. He only had a double-corner silver dollar and three double-cents on him. The woman was wearing a white Indian silk cheongsam, a green suspender vest, red flower silk shorts, flesh-colored stockings, and black high-heeled leather shoes. She was about 20 years old. Neither of them had left a suicide note or business card, so it is temporarily difficult to determine their names, ages, origins, and backgrounds. However, their appearance is quite similar to that of students who have received higher education. As for the reason for their suicide, it is probably related to love. Yesterday afternoon, the Lifesaving Bureau placed the bodies of the man and woman in coffins separately and temporarily left them in the coffin storage room, waiting for relatives to claim them. If no one inquires after three days, the coffins will be transported to the bureau's purchased charity cemetery in Tangwan Township, Minhang, for temporary burial.

=Tang Huan-guang Coveted by Gangsters=

=Blackmail Letter Demanding a Huge Sum of 50,000 Yuan=

Tang Huan-guang, a Cantonese man, lives near the Tangjiawan vegetable market in the western gate of Nanshi. He is of modest means and lives extravagantly. He was targeted by gangsters and received two blackmail letters sent by post on the 30th of last month and the 1st of this month. At that time, Tang wrote a letter as agreed and put it in the designated wastepaper basket, saying, "The amount in the letter is too large" and he could not raise the money. If it was a smaller amount, he could help." The gangsters then sent another letter requesting him to hand over the money in the wastepaper basket next to No. 201, opposite the Yukang cigarette paper shop in Lujiabang Caoxie Bay from 6:00 to 7:00 PM. This was discovered by detective Wang Yongliang of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who immediately reported it to captain Lu Ying. They dispatched leader Gu Liancheng and others, disguised as rickshaw pullers and garbage pickers, together with the police chief of the first section, to lie in ambush around the area. Before long, four people came slowly. As one person reached into the wastepaper basket, Detective Gu and others rushed forward and arrested all four of them. After questioning, they confessed that their names were Zhang Bucai (25 years old, from Funing), Zhu Zhusheng (22 years old, from Tongzhou), Lu Hongfu (28 years old, from Yancheng), and Zhang Zhengtang (43 years old, from Jiangbei). They also confessed the address of their accomplice, Liu Erqun. The original detectives rushed to No. 12 Caoxie Bay Road, Lujiabang, and arrested Liu and escorted him to the team for further investigation.

Woman Cruelly Beats Young Child to Death with Firewood 147

=Secretly Used Black Clothes to Carry the Child's Body Out=

=Returned Alone and Was Discovered by Neighbors=

Yang Xiteng, the second landlord of Tianluyuan candy store at No. 209, Caishi Road, in the French Concession, sublet a three-story pavilion room to Zhao Xia, an old Ningbo woman, last August in the lunar calendar. The woman claimed that her husband had died early, leaving behind a son and a daughter. The son, Xiu Zhang, 19 years old, works as a laundryman in Zhabei. The daughter, Xiuying, 23 years old, married a man named Wang, but Wang died of illness in less than a year. Because Xiuying had no children, she adopted a two-year-old girl named Fudi last year and entrusted her to her mother, Zhao Xia. Xiuying now works as a female worker in a cigarette factory in Zhabei due to her livelihood and does not often visit her mother. However, Xia is naturally fierce and violent. Whenever Fudi cried, she would beat her severely. As time went on, Fudi became frightened and ill. Xia remained indifferent for a month. Recently, her condition became more serious and she was about to die. Until about 8:00 PM the night before last, Fudi suddenly cried again. Xia took a piece of firewood and struck her violently, hitting her head squarely and killing her suddenly. When Xia saw that she had caused a disaster, she remained silent and secretly used a black garment to cover the child's head and carry her out secretly. At that time, the candy store clerk saw her carrying the child out, but did not pay attention to it at first. When he saw Xia returning alone, he became suspicious. Recalling the woman's abuse of the child on weekdays and the woman's hasty departure just now, he became even more suspicious. Out of caution, the second landlord, Yang Xiteng, went to report to the police station. The police chief immediately dispatched a Bao detective to question the woman. Xia was mumbling and unable to form words, so she was taken into the police station. After repeated interrogation, the woman confessed the truth. However, as for the child's body, she claimed that she had entrusted a porter to carry it away for burial for two yuan. However, after the Bao detective went to investigate in person, he never found it. The police station believed that Xia was inhuman and ordered her to be detained, pending delivery to the Second Special District Court for severe punishment.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Exemption from Jiangwan Township Boat Tax 148

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday presented a report to the Municipal Government, saying: "A report is submitted based on the circumstances. On the second day of February, the Jiangwan Branch Office reported that the Fair Brick and Tile Shop and other shops sent a letter saying that the Municipal Finance Bureau had recently sent people to Jiangwan to collect boat tax, which the boat households could not afford, and requested them to forward the exemption. The river channel in the area has been in disrepair for a long time and is increasingly silted up. It can barely be passable during the two floods each month. The boat households have long regarded it as a scourge. All the boats that come and go mostly come from the interior to transport goods for sale, or villagers go to the town to load goods and return. Now, if they are ordered to pay for licenses, the boat households do not know why. Not only is transportation hindered, but also the market is affected. As in the past, small cars traveling within the Wusong area are exempt from licenses for six months. Another example is that there are changed measures that do not require licenses for cattle, sheep, and pigs that are driven in rural areas. All of this proves that the same licensing regulations may be handled flexibly in urban and rural areas. It is reasonable to submit a report for review, transfer it to the Municipal Government, and grant an exemption, which is truly convenient for the public." In view of the fact that the river channel in the district is silted up and rural boats can only pass through two floods each month, it is already difficult for rural towns to trade. If boat taxes are imposed again, rural boats will inevitably disappear, and the market will also stagnate. The branch office proposed to exempt small car donations for six months and livestock does not need a license. It is hoped that the Xiangchuan tax could also be relieved to revive township business. It is appropriate to transfer the situation and hope that the government will review it, order the bureau to approve the exemption of the aforementioned Xiangchuan donations, so as to show the recovery, which is truly convenient for the public.

Hurricane Blows Down Ancient Bell Tower 149

Fortunately, the Bell Body Remains Intact as Before

Shanghai News Agency: The ancient bell tower of the Mingxin Temple in North Bridge is a rare historical site in Shanghai County. It was built in the 14th year of the Ming Dynasty (Wanli). Due to years of disrepair and exposure to wind, frost, and rain, it had long collapsed, leaving only a skeletal frame supporting the ancient bell, which stood tall by the roadside. The bell is made of bronze and weighs 3,600 catties. Gentlemen in Shanghai County have raised funds to build a new bell tower next to the county government. The construction has not yet been completed. Unexpectedly, the old bell suddenly collapsed at 4:00 PM on the 2nd of this month amidst the howling wind and rain. The sound was as loud as thunder in a valley, shocking nearby residents. Fortunately, no pedestrians were passing by, so no one was injured. The bell body is also intact as before, which is also fortunate.

Old Companies Supplement Registration Deadline Ends at the End of the Month 151

No Extension

The Company Law has been implemented since July 1, 1931, for more than two years. Although the number of companies that can apply for registration according to the law has increased day by day, the number of companies that are not familiar with the law, do not know the procedures, and have not registered is still quite large. Therefore, the Ministry of Industry has repeatedly ordered all provincial and municipal bureaus to order all companies in the country to register according to the law within a time limit, and set September 30 of this year as the last deadline. After this extension, there will be no further extension. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, as the government agency in charge of company registration, immediately ordered the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and announced it to all companies in the city after receiving the ministry's order, and required them to register within the time limit. Now, the deadline is approaching. It is heard that there are still many companies in the city that have not registered. When the time comes, the Bureau of Social Affairs will strictly investigate. Once discovered, the directors, supervisors, shareholders, and promoters who are running the company will be fined up to 500 yuan, and they will be strictly investigated. There are not many days left. Companies that have not registered should rush to complete the registration procedures to avoid being fined.

Expansion of Tuberculosis Sanatorium 156

=New Hospital on Hongqiao Road to be Completed Around the End of the Year=

=Sunlight in All Wards from Morning to Dusk=

The Shanghai Tuberculosis Sanatorium, located at 2 Daxi Road in this city, is a specialized hospital for treating tuberculosis. Since implementing various surgical procedures, the treatment results have become even more superior, far exceeding the ordinary internal medicine treatments of the past involving medication and injections. In recent years, in light of societal developments, the original hospital site is no longer sufficient. Therefore, two new-style sanatoriums are being built on Hongqiao Road in western Shanghai. The characteristic feature is that all wards face south, and each room has a separate balcony for reclining and resting. The entire hospital is equipped with fireproof and soundproof installations. In addition to necessary facilities such as operating rooms, electrotherapy rooms, and laboratories, there are also lounges, dining rooms, reading rooms, music rooms, and rooftop gardens. A large solarium is also set up, with sunlight shining in from morning until dusk. In terms of accommodations, in addition to first and second class, there are also free wards and several third-class isolation wards to meet the needs of ordinary patients. All the wards are expected to be completed by the end of this year. Currently, to promote the popularization of tuberculosis prevention and treatment knowledge, the hospital is offering free books published by the Chinese Tuberculosis Society, such as "Tuberculosis Treatment Methods," "Tuberculosis Prevention Methods," and "Special Tuberculosis Treatment Methods," compiled by Ding Fubao and Ding Huikang based on experience. Those who send a letter requesting these books should enclose four cents for postage per book.

They divided the ransom money among themselves. In Tianjin, they kidnapped Liang Huiwu, a wealthy merchant, and killed him after receiving the ransom, burying the body in the garden at 40 Route 38 in the British Concession. They also kidnapped Chen Zhuling, a comprador of Jardine Matheson, killed him after receiving the ransom, and buried the body under the floorboards at 4 Xiangzhi Lane and 4 Baokang Lane in the British Concession. The Tianjin police have already exhumed both bodies. The trial was originally scheduled to begin formally yesterday morning. However, due to the large number of defendants and the complexity of the case, Judge Li Changnian announced that a special court would be opened at 1:00 PM on the 6th for the trial.

Shen Zixiang Recruits in the Name of the Jiangpu Drug Enforcement Office 159

Suspected of Fraud, Arrested by Police

Shen Zixiang, a 21-year-old from Ningbo Feng hua, formerly worked in education. Recently, Shen suddenly claimed to be the director of the West District Office of the Jiangpu County Drug Enforcement Office of Jiangsu Province. He rented a room at 288 Maigen Road, the location of the Shenmei Girls' Middle School, and placed an advertisement in the News on the 26th of last month, recruiting 25 male and female staff members with a monthly salary of 30 yuan. However, applicants were required to pay an application fee of one yuan each, and the official examination was scheduled for the 3rd of this month. Since the advertisement was published, many unemployed people flocked to register and pay the fee. In the past few days, the number reached over a hundred people, all of whom were personally received by Shen, who issued receipts instructing them to wait for the examination. However, this matter came to the attention of the Jiangsu Provincial Drug Enforcement Office, which stated that it did not have a West District Office and had not entrusted Shen Zixiang to publish advertisements for recruitment. It was suspected that he was falsely using the name to collect money. Therefore, Supervising Officer Shao Ziying was specially dispatched to Shanghai the day before yesterday to conduct a secret investigation. He also went to Shen at the Fanmei Middle School, posing as an applicant and paying the application fee of one yuan on the spot. At that time, Zhang Shunnian and Li Zhichao were also there to register and pay the fee. Shen issued receipts to all of them. Supervising Officer Shao confirmed the facts and reported to the Gordon Road Police Station, which dispatched Chinese Detective Pi Shaochang and Western Detective Lai Yin to arrest Shen. They confiscated a letter of appointment, three receipt books, a newspaper, a notice, and a bundle of career battle letters, and brought them to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Summary Court of the First Special District Court. Police Lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated the above facts and presented all the confiscated items as evidence, accusing the defendant Shen Zixiang of fraud under Article 363, Section 1 of the Criminal Law. Supervising Officer Shao Ziying of the Jiangsu Provincial Drug Enforcement Office testified that after reading the defendant's advertisement claiming to be the director of the West District Office and recruiting staff, he was sent to Shanghai to investigate and also registered and paid one yuan to apply. However, all branch office directors in our office are appointed by Section Chief Shen alone, and he has not instructed the defendant to publish advertisements for recruitment. The director of the Jiangpu County Drug Enforcement Office is Dong Changfu, etc. Zhang Shunnian and Li Zhichao also testified that they went to report and paid one yuan each, and the defendant issued receipts. When questioned, Shen Zixiang confessed that he was appointed as the director of the West District Office by Team Leader Wang of the Jiangpu County Drug Enforcement Office and agreed with Director Dong Changfu of the office to handle the West District drug enforcement matters, stipulating that he would report 50 yuan per month in addition to all expenses. Therefore, he published advertisements to recruit male and female staff, and each person would pay an application fee of one yuan. However, if they were not selected, the application fee would be refunded. He stated that he had contacted Director Dong about this matter, and Dong was the branch director of Jiangpu County, so the Jiangsu Provincial Headquarters would naturally not know about it. Judge Wu Xiangzu reviewed the confession and believed that the investigation of Dong Changfu was very important to this case, so it was necessary to postpone the hearing. He ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and wait for Team Leader Wang to be summoned to court for further questioning at a later date.

Tea Room Employee Commits Suicide by Poison 161

Ni Yongqing, a 23-year-old tea room employee from Huzhou, was employed at 1 Guanhua Lane, Route Lafayette in the French Concession. House Collapse Injures People in Jiangwan 162

A vacant building opposite Dong Yuanyü Medical Garden on Wan'an Bridge West Main Street in Jiangwan Town suddenly collapsed at 2:00 AM during a storm, hitting the Xu family teahouse next door and injuring two workers. The seriously injured were sent to Jiangwan Hospital for treatment, while those with minor injuries bandaged themselves. In addition, the Great Buddha Hall, commonly known as the Daxiong Hall, of the Sanmen Temple also had its high walls and large stones, which had remained after being bombed by the Japanese during the January 28th Incident, collapse onto the road that night. Fortunately, no pedestrians were affected. It is hoped that those responsible for municipal affairs will strictly control dangerous walls and buildings.

Wang Awu, a 10-year-old from Pudong, was walking on Route Foch at approximately 5:00 PM yesterday when a car with license plate number 1144 came speeding towards him. The child was unable to avoid it and was knocked to the ground, suffering severe head injuries. A policeman found him and rushed the injured child to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, due to the severity of his injuries, he had already died upon arrival. The body was transferred to the coroner's office for examination. The car driver who caused the accident has been detained at the police station pending investigation.

Swindling Diamond Ring for Mortgage and Spending 164

Light Fine of 60 Yuan

Wang Zhen, a Chaozhou shop assistant at the Ruikang Pawnshop at 3 Xingchang Lane, East Xinqiao Street in the French Concession, purchased four diamond rings worth 2,170 yuan at a certain pawnshop at 1338 North Sichuan Road on the 31st of last month. Wu Dayou, an employee of that pawnshop, delivered the goods to Ruikang Pawnshop, where Wang issued a receipt promising to pay for them later. Unexpectedly, Wang took the diamond rings to the Anyu Pawnshop on Sanma Road, mortgaged them for over 2,000 yuan, and spent the money. Wu Dayou found out and demanded payment, but Wang ignored him. Therefore, he reported to the police station, and Wang was arrested and sent to the Second Special District Court on charges of fraud. Yesterday, Judge Wu interrogated him in the Eighth Criminal Court. The police lawyer explained the case, and Wang Zhen confessed to pawning the rings and spending the money. Judge Sun reviewed the confession and sentenced Wang Zhen to a fine of 60 yuan for fraud as a warning.

August Report on Charitable Activities of the Pushan Villa 167

In August, Pushan Villa collected and buried a total of 119 large coffins and 2,191 small coffins in both the northern and southern Chinese-administered areas of the concessions. Of these, the main villa collected 36 large coffins and 1,324 small coffins in Zhabei and other areas. The Xieqiao branch villa collected and buried a total of 442 small coffins from the French Concession, the Nanshi area, and various charitable halls. According to the notices from various police stations and health departments of the Public Concession, a total of 58 large coffins and 425 small coffins containing unclaimed bodies and abandoned infant corpses were collected and buried within the concession. The Red Cross Society of China's hospitals sent 11 large coffins, Tongren Hospital sent 6 large coffins, the Emergency Epidemic Hospital sent 2 large coffins, and the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital sent 6 large coffins. A total of 1,005 large and small coffins were distributed. All the above corpses were transported to the Yihào in Dachang, Tangqiao, and other places for burial and marked for future identification. In addition, the Bai Shizi Pushan Hospital on Xinmin Road provided medical consultations and medications to a total of 7,140 people in August.

Weather Report 177

The Zikawei Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The weather here is clear. Around Shandong, over the Yellow Sea, and along the coast here, there are gentle to northwest winds. The weather around northern Japan is extremely severe due to a hurricane moving northeastward. Northwest of the Caroline Islands, the atmospheric pressure is dropping. The wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 89.2 degrees and the lowest was 72.3 degrees. Local News

[IP>Record of Trial of the Examination Case

Interrogation of Xie Ying, Xie Zhen, and Zhang Jieliang 183

The defendants claimed there was no exchange of money.

On July 17 of this year, the Shanghai Education Bureau held a summer graduation examination for various schools. It was discovered at the test site at Great China University that Xie Ying, a high school student from Jianguo Middle School, had used illegal means to obtain the test questions in advance, which caused the students from various schools taking the test to protest and boycott the test. The authorities immediately reported this to the Public Security Bureau, and Xie Ying, his brother Xie Zhen, and Zhang Jieliang were detained and sent to the Shanghai District Court. After preliminary examination by the prosecutor, they were formally charged with crimes such as encroachment and incitement. A trial was held, Zhang Jieliang was taken into custody, Xie Ying was sent to New Puyu Hall for medical treatment due to illness, and Xie Zhen was released on bail of 500 yuan. Yesterday morning at 9 o'clock, Judge Qian Chengjun of the criminal court opened the third courtroom for the trial. Each defendant hired a lawyer to defend them in court. Judge Qian ordered the case to be re-examined. First, Xie Ying was brought before the court. He stated that he was 20 years old, from Haining, Zhejiang, and was studying in the second year of high school at Jianguo Middle School in Zhabei, Shanghai, and lived on campus. He was asked if he had ever been in legal trouble before, and he replied no. He was asked who Xie Zhen was, and he replied that he was his older brother. He was asked about his brother's occupation, and he replied that his brother worked in the advertising department of the Central Daily News in Nanjing. He was asked that since he was a student in the third year of high school at Jianguo Middle School, who had given him the examination questions. He replied that his older brother had given them to him. He was asked what day it was, and he replied June 13. He was asked how many questions there were, and he replied three, for English, history, and biology, and his brother gave them to him in person because his family's financial situation was tight and he had dropped out of school for two years. He was asked if he had requested these questions from his brother or if his brother had given them to him. He replied that he had not requested them. He was asked if he knew Zhang Jieliang, and he replied that he did. He was asked that since he was a third-year high school student, how could he do such a thing and if he knew what Zhang Jieliang did for a living. He replied that he knew that he worked in a printing factory in Nanjing. Xie Zhen was then brought before the court. He stated that he was 32 years old, from Haining, and currently resided at the Zhongzhou Hotel on Simalu. He currently worked in the advertising department of the Central Daily News in Nanjing. Xie Ying was his younger brother. He was asked how many questions he had given to his brother, and he replied three, for history, biology, and English. He was asked where he had obtained these questions, and he replied that Zhang Jieliang had written them out. He was asked if he had given these questions to his brother, and he replied yes. He was asked why he had given them to his brother, and he replied that he hoped he would graduate. He was asked if Zhang Jieliang was a relative or a friend, and he replied that he was from the same hometown. He was asked when Zhang Jieliang had given him the questions, and he replied on the morning of June 12. He was asked if he had paid any money, and he replied no. Zhang Jieliang stated that he was 20 years old, from Haining, and worked as a proofreader at a printing factory in Nanjing. He was asked if he knew Xie Ying and Xie Zhen, and he replied that he knew Xie Zhen but did not know Xie Ying. He was asked how many questions he had copied out, and he replied three, for English, biology, and history. He was asked when he had shown them to Xie Zhen, and he replied before noon on June 12. He was asked why he had copied them out, and he replied that he was curious. He was asked if he knew who Xie Zhen had given them to, and he replied that he did not. He was asked if he had copied them out because he was a proofreader, and he replied yes. He was asked why he, and not the Education Bureau proofreader, was proofreading. He replied that they proofread first, and then the Education Bureau proofread. He was asked if Xie Zhen had asked him to do it beforehand, and he replied no. He was asked if he had asked Xie Zhen for money, and he replied no. The judge ruled that the case still required witnesses to be summoned. Xie Zhen was still released on his original bail, and Xie Ying and Zhang Jieliang were ordered to post written bail of 500 yuan each and await further instructions.

Chen Xuanshan Discusses the Education Situation in the Public Concession 184

The newly appointed Deputy Director of the Education Department of the Municipal Council, Mr. Chen Xuanshan, assumed his duties on September 1. Yesterday, the reporter visited Mr. Chen at the Education Department of the Municipal Council to inquire about the education situation in the concession. According to his account, the number of school-age children in the concession has been increasing in recent years, leading to a shortage of capacity in the existing primary and secondary schools. In order to popularize education in the concession, the Municipal Council plans to add primary and secondary schools year by year within the possible scope, according to the original plan, so that school-age children in the concession can avoid being turned away. Regarding subsidies for private schools, negotiations are currently underway with the Municipal Education Bureau. Once a result is obtained, it can be implemented. However, the Municipal Council will designate the use of the subsidy funds. The existing primary and secondary schools in the concession are mostly makeshift due to limited funding, and various facilities are also incomplete. The Municipal Council also plans to reform and enrich them.

China Science Society Raises Funds for Biological Research Institute 185

The total fund amount is 500,000 yuan

The Board of Directors is responsible for the custody of the funds.

The Biological Research Institute of the China Science Society was established in the 11th year of the Republic of China. After ten years of hard work, it has earned international recognition. Now, in order to expand the Institute's affairs and enhance its scale, we are launching a fundraising campaign. The methods are as follows:

Fundraising Methods 186

(1) The total amount of the fund to be raised is set at 500,000 yuan in national currency. (2) Those who donate large sums that are not easily collected at once may pay in installments. (3) Those who donate 500,000 yuan alone may use their title as the name of the fund and may also designate three other people (including themselves, four in total) to be directors of the fund. A full-body bronze statue will be permanently placed within the fund to commemorate their admiration. When the Institute has new buildings, the new building will be named after them to perpetuate their virtue. All publications of the Society and the Institute will be given to them for life, and their name will be permanently engraved on the title page of the Institute's publications. (4) Those who donate 100,000 yuan or more may propose the name of the fund, and they will automatically be directors of the fund. A full-body statue will be placed on the Institute's bronze monument, and when there are new buildings, the main hall will be named after their title. All publications of the Society will be given to them for life to express our gratitude. (5) Those who donate 10,000 yuan or more will have a half-body statue placed on the Institute's bronze monument, and their name will be used as the name of each laboratory in the Institute to commemorate them. They will be alternate directors of the fund, and the Institute will also present them with a plaque to express our gratitude. (6) Those who donate 1,000 yuan or more will have their portrait hung in the Institute and their name engraved on the Institute's bronze monument to leave a permanent memorial. They will also be supporting members of the Society. (7) Those who donate 100 yuan or more will have their name engraved on the Institute's bronze monument to commemorate them. (8) After receiving the donation, in addition to issuing a receipt, the Society will publish the names and amounts of the donors in batches in the newspaper to express our gratitude and demonstrate our integrity. (9) In accordance with the Ministry of Education's promulgated regulations on rewarding financial assistance for education, the Society will submit a request to the Ministry of Education to reward those who donate large sums to promote their virtue. (10) These methods and regulations will be implemented after being approved by the Council of the Society. Matters not covered may be supplemented by the Council at any time.

Custody Methods 187

(1) This fund will be entrusted to a reputable bank for safekeeping by the Biological Research Institute Fund Board of Directors specially established by the Society. Before the Fund Board of Directors is established, the Society's Board of Directors will temporarily act on its behalf. (2) The Fund Board of Directors will report the accounts and handled matters annually and print them into a special booklet to be distributed to each donor. (3) This fund may not be used; only the interest may be used. The use of the interest must first be approved by the Fund Board of Directors. (4) The Fund Board of Directors is temporarily set at nine directors. The Director of the Institute and those who donate 100,000 yuan or more are naturally directors. Those who donate 10,000 yuan or more are alternate directors. Donating directors will be sufficient with six people, and the remaining two will be mutually recommended by the Society's directors.

Municipal Education Bureau Forbids Zhishen Elementary School from Falsely Claiming Approval for Establishment 188

The private Zhishen Elementary School at the intersection of West Avenue and Talas Road was recently opened and immediately changed its name. Painter Li Yunyan Departs for Overseas 189

Painter Li Yunyan is skilled in Western painting and industrial art design, and his traditional Chinese paintings are refined and ethereal. His plum blossom paintings are especially renowned. He is departing for Japan today on the Nagasaki Maru to study art there and continue his research on industrial art design. In the future, he will surely make great contributions to China's industrial sector. It is reported that he is also taking dozens of his masterpiece plum blossom paintings to exhibit in Tokyo to promote national culture.

Dr. Gu Hailou Returns to China 190

Gu Hailou, from Jiangsu Province, studied at the Faculty of Medicine of the National Tongji University. In the spring of the 18th year of the Republic of China, he went to Germany to specialize in dentistry. In the summer of the 21st year, he passed the German National Examination at the University of Erlangen in Bavaria. In November of the same year, he obtained a Doctorate in Dental Medicine with excellent grades. He then went to the Faculty of Dentistry at the University of Nancy in France to work as an assistant instructor. He has now returned to China from Europe and plans to practice medicine in Shanghai.

Vocational Education Society Establishes Rural Service Specialization Course 191

The China Vocational Education Society runs rural education programs, which use little money and achieve great results, earning sympathy from all sides. Recently, feeling the lack of rural talent, it established a Rural Service Specialization Course. It purchased more than 100 mu of land in the countryside of Caohejing in the western suburbs of Shanghai and developed it into a farm, designating more than 30 villages as practice sites. It recruits high school graduates with experience in serving rural areas and provides them with two years of special training in education, economics, and self-governance to cultivate rural service talents with both knowledge and skills to meet social needs. Since it started advertising for enrollment, many people have submitted self-written essays and applied for registration, and many have resigned from their original positions to request admission. The Admissions Office has carefully reviewed and responded to each application separately. It is understood that the course also stipulates that students will be assigned positions by the Society upon graduation. If their abilities are insufficient, they can still stay on the farm to work and live self-sufficiently to avoid unemployment. Those who are interested in rural careers and seek a way out for the nation can attach a two-cent stamp and send a letter to the Society at No. 80 Hualong Road, Shanghai, to request the course brochure.

Shen Bao Series: The Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan for Agriculture Published 199

In the current climate of China's rural revitalization movement, the publication of this book is of great significance. Ten years ago, the Soviet Union's drought and famine were worse than the current state of decline in China's countryside, but the Soviet Union's six-year recovery period and first five-year plan have achieved results worth mirroring. This book is originally authored by Yakovlev of the Soviet Agricultural Committee and provides a detailed description of the origins of the Five-Year Plan for Agriculture. Countries around the world are competing to translate it. It is now translated by Mr. Gao Zhixiang and includes five of the most valuable recent agricultural data, with eight illustrations. It is an essential reference for those studying rural issues. The actual price is 50 cents. It is published by the distribution department of this newspaper. During the autumn school opening period, the special price is for one month. Purchases of ten or more copies are calculated at 70% of the original price.

Jiangsu Fifth District Games Concludes in Storm 206

Shanghai Wins Half of the Eight Championships and Takes the Overall Championship

Accidents Occur in Ball Games, Championships Evenly Distributed

Ding Yuhua of Shanghai Wins First Place in Women's Athletics

The Jiangsu Fifth Administrative District Games opened on September 1. Details of the track and field events on the first day have been reported in various newspapers. The reporter predicted that the meeting would be postponed due to the wind and rain on the 2nd and 3rd, so he went there yesterday. Unexpectedly, the ball games were held in the storm, and the players left unhappily due to disputes between the players. The details are recorded as follows:

IP>Total Track and Field Points

Group Part 207

(1) The first place in the total score of men's track events is Shanghai with 43 points, the second is Nanhui with 28 points, and the third is Chuansha with 12 points. (2) Nanhui and Chuansha each have 28 points in the total score of men's field events. According to the regulations, Nanhui has more first place finishes, so the championship goes to Nanhui, and the second place is Shanghai with 21 points. (3) The first place in the total score of women's track and field events is Shanghai with 421 points, the second is Chuansha with 5 points, and the third is Nanhui with 0 points.

Personal Scores 208

(1) Men's Track Total Points: First Place - Song En (South), Wang Changsheng (Shanghai), 13 points each; Second Place - Tao Shaosheng (South), Huang Hanru (Shanghai), 10 points each; Third Place - Zheng Guanhai (Sichuan), 6 points. (2) Men's Field Total Points: First Place - Wu Wanglin (South), 15 points; Second Place - Zhou Changxiao (Sichuan), 13 points; Third Place - Huang Gaoxi (Shanghai), 7 points. (3) Women's Track and Field Total Points: First Place - Ding Yuhua (Shanghai), 20 points; Second Place - Ding Lianfang (Shanghai), 14 points; Third Place - Wu Jinbao (Shanghai), 7 points. Track and field overall team score: First place - Shanghai; Individual first place - Wu Yulin; Women's individual first place - Ding Yuhua.

Game Situation 209

▲Dispute Occurred: This time, the association's ball games included four types: football, basketball, volleyball, and tennis. Chuansha only participated in basketball and volleyball. Therefore, apart from basketball and volleyball using an elimination system, both football and tennis were matches between Shanghai and Nanhui. Considering the power balance, Shanghai was expected to win. This led to the demoralization of athletes from Nanhui and Chuansha counties, which was the main reason for the dispute. On the 2nd of this month, with wind and rain, the competition committee announced that volleyball would be played in the morning. Shanghai athletes requested a postponement due to the strong wind and light balls. Shanghai refused to join during the draw, and the organizing committee decided to play at 12 o'clock. Shanghai county athletes, as it was lunchtime, did not arrive. The organizing committee declared Shanghai county's forfeit, causing resentment.

▲Emergency Meeting: The organizing committee convened an emergency meeting at 1 pm that afternoon. All committee members attended. Chairman Cao Zhenfei immediately decided that the basketball games would start at 4 pm on the 2nd for the first game, and 5:15 pm for the second. Tennis would start at 9 am on the 3rd, and football at 1 pm on the 3rd. However, regarding the volleyball issue, Nanchuan counties insisted that Shanghai county had forfeited, while Shanghai county firmly opposed, leading to no resolution.

▲Basketball Game: At 4 pm on the 3rd, the three counties' basketball athletes followed the organizing committee's decision, each preparing for battle. Despite the wind and rain, none were negligent. After the draw, Shanghai and Chuansha faced off first. At the sound of the whistle, both sides formed their formations and ended at 5:10 pm. As a result, Shanghai defeated Chuansha. (The association official in charge of records refused to disclose the score.) Shanghai county athletes, having just finished a fierce battle, were exhausted. However, as the time for the second game had arrived, they reluctantly fought and were defeated by Nanhui. The basketball championship was thus won by Nanhui.

▲Opposing Postponement: The wind and rain did not subside on the 3rd. Shanghai county proposed postponing the games, but was opposed by Chuansha and Nanhui counties. Consequently, at 9 am, tennis athletes from Nanhui and Nanchuan entered the field, but the referees were suddenly absent, leading to problems. At 1 pm for the football game, the referees were again absent. The athletes could only wait for a resolution helplessly.

▲Distributing Prizes: The ball games, football, volleyball, and tennis, all had no results, as mentioned above. Nanchuan counties neither advocated for a postponement nor insisted on returning to their counties on the 3rd. This made resolving the championship issue impossible. The organizing committee held another meeting. As a result, the three unplayed championships were evenly distributed. The volleyball championship was awarded to Chuansha, the tennis championship to Nanhui, and the football championship to Shanghai. The turmoil subsided. In the afternoon, the three counties' athletes boarded cars after Commissioner Cao presented the awards. They departed in the pouring rain. During the farewell, some cheered, while others cursed from the three cars, truly an interesting final entertainment.

The Municipal Government Orders the National Arts Museum to Postpone the Second National Arts Examination 211

Due to Conflict with the National Games Schedule

Held at the Beijing Sports Field on the 10th and 20th

The Municipal Government of this city, previously approved the Central National Arts Museum's telegram, stating that the second National Arts Examination was originally scheduled to be held on the 10th of the 20th year, but was postponed due to national crisis, and both requests were telegraphed and approved. Now, this museum cites the case and requests the National Government to approve the holding of the second National Examination on October 16th of this year, immediately after the conclusion of the National Games competition at its venue. It should be requested to notify the affiliated units and inform the number of applicants for the National Examination before September 10th, with the number not exceeding 30 people. Once the athletes are on their way, please issue a certificate of proof for them to negotiate with transportation agencies for half-price fares on domestic railways and ships, in order to show consideration. In addition to separate telegrams, it is urgently requested to investigate and handle the matter. Furthermore, a telegram from the Central National Arts Museum stated that the second National Arts Examination, originally scheduled to be held on October 16th of this year at the Central Sports Field, has already been telegraphed to you. Due to the simultaneous opening of the National Games, the time and location are slightly conflicting. After discussion by the preparatory committee for the second National Examination of this museum, it was decided to postpone it to October 20th and hold it at the Public Sports Field in Beijing. In addition to reporting for record, it is urgently requested to transfer the order to comply. The government immediately issued an order to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to cooperate with the Municipal National Arts Museum to comply.

Spring and Autumn

Solving the Sexual Desires of Prisoners 220

— Drunkard

The judicial authorities have already decided on a method to solve the sexual desires of prisoners. However, according to my humble opinion, there are still some points that need to be discussed. I hereby raise them below:

(1) Violating the Eugenics Law: Germany's Hitler recently promulgated the "Eugenics Law" to improve the people's personality and ensure healthy bodies. All undesirable elements in society, such as criminals, the mentally ill, and those with hereditary diseases, must be prevented from reproducing or have their reproductive functions eliminated. This law will be implemented from January next year. Our country has a vast territory and a large population, so it is not possible to imitate this law. However, prisoners are naturally prevented from reproducing during their sentences. Allowing couples to meet once every two or three months is no different from encouraging reproduction. The children born to cruel and licentious people in harsh environments will naturally have no hope of "excellence," and their hereditary nature is truly frightening. Is this not in great contradiction with the "Eugenics Law"?

(2) No Need to Solve: As the saying goes, "Satiety breeds lust." This shows that a person's sexual desires only have a chance to be stimulated in a pleasant situation. As for prisoners who have committed crimes and are in confinement, they are experiencing the taste of iron bars. Their bodies and minds are suffering deeply. Where do they have the leisure to think about the "playing the lute under the yellow plum tree" kind of work? Therefore, it seems that there is no need to solve this sexual desire problem on their behalf.

(3) Unequal Treatment: This decree was originally intended to reward well-behaved prisoners. However, it is limited to formal couples. Other prisoners without husbands or wives, or those who are not formally married, are still left out in the cold and do not receive this treatment. Then, this solution is not a thorough solution and will instead arouse psychological inequalities and sexual urges among the other prisoners. Moreover, there are many other ways to reward them, so why use this difficult-to-universalize sexual activity as a reward?

The above three points do not seem to have been considered humanely. I have specially written them out for legal scholars to study. In short, solving the sexual desires problem seems to be "neglecting the root and pursuing the branch," which is not the most important plan at present. The most important thing is to improve the problems of diet, sanitation, hygiene, and all other long-standing abuses. Then, the prisoners will be able to receive real benefits.

Enlightenment from Catching Flies 221

— Nineteen

Autumn has arrived, and there are especially many autumn flies. This morning, during breakfast, I saw three or four flies flying around the table. I knew that they were our great enemies, so I quickly grabbed a fly swatter, aimed, and wanted to wipe them out in one fell swoop. Who knew that with a "whack," only one enemy died under my iron fist, and the rest escaped to who knows where. Although I couldn't help but feel a little disappointed at the time, I still sat quietly at the table, waiting for an opportunity to move. But they, like fish that slipped through the net, never came into my sight again. I couldn't help but throw down the fly swatter and let out a long sigh.

Flies are ignorant animals and seem to have no cunning. However, since humans invented the fly swatter, they have become more and more clever day by day. This is beyond our expectations. For example, in this fly-catching incident, one was deceived, and the rest harbored vigilance and avoided me. This is clear evidence. As the saying goes, "Those who have schemes must have cunning." This saying is very reasonable. To extend it further, the fly swatter is just a tool to treat the symptoms of catching flies. Trying to cure the root cause and purify the source with it will not have much effect. Because treating the symptoms is only a temporary solution, while curing the root cause and purifying the source is a permanent plan and will never be so simple. Therefore, I must admit that it was my mistake to think that I could wipe out all the flies with one swat. Catching flies is like this, and why should other things be any different? So finally, I want to quote a classical writer's style and say, "Gentlemen, from this, you can gain enlightenment!"

Inspired by a "Maid's" Beating 222

— Fu Yizhi

Lincoln believed that "slavery is based on unjust and bad policies," so he advocated that slave states join the Union. Although it triggered the historically famous Civil War, in the end, the Northern states achieved the final victory. Finally, on New Year's Day in 1863, he issued a declaration and implemented the emancipation of black slaves in the Southern states. This is indeed a memorable event in the history of human civilization.

China also often boasts of being an ancient civilized country in the world, but the buying and selling of slaves has not yet been abolished. Although with the high tide of the revolution, there was once a feverish shout of "liberation," names like "family members" and "book boys" seem to no longer exist. As for whether they exist in reality, that is another question. But the name of "maid" and the fact of keeping maids exist everywhere and cannot be concealed. However, this name and fact only exist in the groups of the bourgeois class.

Recently, I have rashly stepped on the edge of the small bourgeois lifestyle circle. What has made me feel most inexplicable is the number of female servants and bought maids in this lifestyle circle, which is beyond my usual imagination. Of course, more somber and tragic facts are also discovered. Not long ago, a "maid" in a certain house number ran away, implicating the "maid" of the next-door neighbor (a seventeen or eighteen-year-old girl) as a suspect. As a result, the neighbor's "maid" suffered, and was brutally beaten by her master for a minor reason. At the very least, she had to kneel for three hours, but she was not allowed to cry. Recently, people have not been allowed to watch. Occasionally, one or two dull-headed humanitarians stand up and shout a few "no's," but that's all they do. It is said that this little girl is waiting for someone to rescue her. If there is a swordsman-like figure who is willing to unleash his instincts and rescue this innocent and pitiful maid, I think his achievements are no less than Lincoln's.

Here, the problem has happened again. It is not difficult for us to rescue her from the cage. However, after she is out of the cage, what about her clothing, food, and shelter? Moreover, she is not the only maid, and she is probably not the only one being tortured. According to Kiku Kawa's explanation, nurses, elementary school teachers, etc., can all be called silver slaves. Then, slaves already account for the absolute majority in society, and I am still one of them in this slave circle. I am too busy to save myself, how dare I rashly talk about saving others? As I write this, I can't help but sigh repeatedly!

City Moon 223

— Yan Chonglou

That clear like water, that bright like a mirror, that pure like a virgin's heart, isn't that the moon deeply imprinted in our hearts?

In the natural countryside, whenever the god of night spreads its wings, our moon gradually emerges from the mountains. It bathes in the light air, revealing a gentle smile. Then, the forests, streams, lawns, etc., are all covered with a layer of silver brilliance. All living things are active. Even the tiny mosquitoes sing and dance for it.

In the bustling city, electric lights and neon lights shine day and night. Tall buildings block the surroundings, preventing me from seeing the longed-for moon all night long. Sometimes I have to raise my feet and crane my neck to see that it is cramped on the roof, revealing a sad face. I want to comfort it and tell it my longing, but at this time, a burst of thick smoke will come out of the chimney on the roof, and then I can't even see its sad face!

The same moon appears dim in the city. "Moon! Don't sigh because of sadness, and don't grieve because of disappointment. You should know that this environment is fundamentally unsuitable for you. This is a world that needs another kind of moon."

From Hot to Cold 224

— Yi Qiu

The climate has changed from hot to cold; the scenery will change from prosperity to desolation; the blood of animals has also changed from boiling to tranquility. This is the phenomenon that should occur when the hot summer passes and the new autumn arrives in the world.

In the past, the sun was scorching, and people were so hot that they had nowhere to go, relying entirely on ice cream and fresh orange juice to calm the fire in their hearts. Now that it is autumn, these things are no longer needed. Prepare to admire the bright autumn moon and eat the round mooncakes!

In the past, foreign insults were becoming more urgent every day, and the people of the country were filled with righteous indignation, relying entirely on shouting the slogan "Resist Japan and save the country" to relieve the anger in their chests. Now, the puppet troops are being incorporated one after another, and the Chahar incident has been resolved. The overall situation has been determined. The term "Resist Japan and save the country" is no longer mentioned frequently. Everyone is going to live in peace and prepare for singing and dancing!

The climate has changed from hot to cold, and people's blood has changed from hot to cold. Everything in China has also changed from hot to cold. Ah! Autumn is cold! Autumn is cold! No wonder the earth is so tranquil.

Women's Paradise

Cultivating Beauty 226

When I was a girl, an old nanny once told me earnestly, "Beauty is only skin deep." I always felt that this saying was superficial and not to be believed. Later, one day, my uncle added this to what the old nanny said: "But ugliness goes to the bone." Only then was its original meaning complete, and I suddenly understood, gaining considerable comfort. It is known that if girls like to talk, they should preserve this little vanity.

Nowadays, most mothers encourage their girls to cultivate beauty. This is indeed a good method because if girls pay considerable attention to their complexion, skin, teeth, and exercise when they are young, then they will certainly have a beautiful appearance and a healthy physique when they grow up. And there is also a most important point, which is that they will have a considerable understanding and proper maintenance of themselves.

I would like to guide every girl to pay attention to her hair. Spending ten minutes brushing hair every morning and evening is worth doing. I would like to encourage them to protect their skin, not only relying on the help of lotions or cosmetics, but also relying on the effects of practicing deep breathing and exercise, so that the skin reaches the state of being fair, smooth, moist, and tender. More fresh air will certainly make the skin fair, smooth, moist, and tender most effectively and noticeably. Now, sports in schools are very beneficial to children. However, if mothers and children practice prescribed exercises once every morning, such as calisthenics, then a pleasant life during the day and a beautiful appearance have already been successfully created.

As for teeth, schools also pay close attention to them, and there are considerable examinations. Pearl-like white teeth are indeed the glory of every girl, but toothbrushing training should begin in early childhood. When a child can just hold a toothbrush, they should be taught how to use the toothbrush, and then told why the mouth should be preserved in such a cautious, strict, clean, and healthy state. If mothers pay a little attention to their children's teeth and mouth, then half of their future illnesses can be avoided. Rinsing the mouth should also be taught to children, and they should also be taught to use a nasal irrigation method; by following this method, many severe colds can also be avoided.

Limited vanity can no longer be regarded as a sin, so finally, I am more willing to guide every girl to pay attention to her clothes, to give her an interest in clothing, to teach her to find the colors and styles that best suit her, and to let her draw up a clothing list when she is first able to manage her own clothes. At the same time, I would like to guide her to clean and organize her clothes, to teach her how to brush, how to fold, how to put away, and how to store them. (I would like to guide boys in the same way, knowing that a future daughter-in-law will definitely thank me very much.)

Clothes and Health 227

— Pei Yu

The important effect of clothing on the health of your children cannot be emphasized enough.

Clothes that are put on without buttons have many different disadvantages, the most obvious of which is making the chest narrow, the shoulders low and rounded, resulting in poor breathing and lack of nutrition. Tight and round collars easily cause earaches in children, and tight elastic waistbands can cause indigestion.

There are many causes of back pain in children, the most common of which is the use of suspenders. Suspenders that are so short and pull up the entire unbalanced body are most effective at causing back pain in children. Mothers should see that children who use suspenders are not very happy to play.

Children who use suspenders are not very happy to play.

Shoes are also very important; if the heels are too high (referring to leather shoes), then the child's center of gravity will often lean forward, which is enough to make the muscles of the calf excessively elongated. Excessive elongation means excessive exertion, and the result is that it is easy to have sprains.

Clothes that are too loose should also be avoided. So-called clothes that are too loose include work clothes that are so loose that they constantly slip off the shoulders, sleeves that are so long that they drag past the wrists, and socks whose tops constantly fall down.

According to Japanese estimates, the second US cotton report will increase by about 13.36 million bales, and the new cotton on the market in various regions is quite abundant, and farmers are selling at very low prices due to economic difficulties.

Minbang's Handling is Waiting and Seeing

Yesterday, new Guest Indica rice continued to be transported from Hunan and Huocao, and there were still several batches of new rice from Hunan being transported, because the production price was already low, and small vendors were all trying to install it, so there will be arrivals in the near future. There are also many new rice from Nanjing transported by train to the local area of Nanjing and Anhui Province in Jiangbei. Therefore, people's minds are weak, and because the Communist bandits are spreading in various places in Fujian Province, and commercial stagnation, Minbang has the stomach but does not dare to handle it smoothly.
