Flour Standard Begins to Stabilize and Then Falls 243

After the opening of the flour market yesterday morning, the prices in each month showed a trend of first stabilizing and then falling. Because the quotation of foreign wheat was suspended and there were no reports, the market sentiment was still stable at the beginning. After that, the sales in Tianjin stagnated again after the market price increased by a few points. This situation is the main reason for the sluggishness of the flour market. Therefore, some large and small factories frequently issued blocks for the near and distant futures, and those in the Tianjin gang who were familiar with the situation also returned and issued a lot, so the market immediately saw a sharp decline. Until the afternoon opening, the current month fell by 0.065 yuan, and October fell to 0.0925 yuan, which was 0.03-0.04 yuan lower than the previous day's closing price. However, after this, the market sentiment gradually improved again. It was heard that Nandian Bang had always been bullish and gradually bought in, and some factories also came out to absorb and raise the price, so it rebounded by 0.01 yuan compared to the lowest price. The market is actually not prosperous, and the inventory on the market is abundant. If there is no effect, there should be a final short-selling situation. The current month fell by 0.0225 yuan compared to the previous day, October fell by 0.0175 yuan, November fell by 0.015 yuan, December fell by 0.0075 yuan, January fell by 0.002, and February fell by 0.0125 yuan.

In the Hurricane 244

— Tian Fang

Gloomy weather, howling wind, pattering rain, blowing and falling incessantly. Chaotic clouds billow overhead, the sun not showing a sliver of light. Signal lights flash on the rivers and seas, black signal balls hoisted. Turbulent waves churn in the Huangpu River, swallowing the wild cries of all sizes of steam whistles on the river; many ships quietly moor along the banks; the trees by the river sway madly as if about to fly away with the wind. The bustling Bund, with its normally shuttling ships and carriages, is now sparse and desolate, transformed into a world of biting winds and cold rain. People hurrying along the roads wear grim faces, as if burdened by immense worries; this is the eve of the approaching hurricane.

Indeed, people completely lose control in the face of the terrifying threat of nature! As you walk along the Huangpu River, turbulent waves incessantly crash against the shore, the strong wind, mixed with rustling rain, comes from all directions, enveloping you, making it impossible to move or breathe. What you see are dark clouds and waves, what you hear are the sounds of wind and rain; all external threats plunge your entire mood into an abyss of terror, like a small boat that has lost its oar and is forced to flee.

The hurricane intensifies, the echoes heard strike the walls as if preparing to destroy all buildings. People generally worry about the future horrors, looking up to the sky, asking when this gloom will clear. However, the technicians at the Observatory know, they can tell us how many miles this hurricane travels per hour, when it will leave us, without the slightest hesitation. Yes, the hurricane is bound to come, and when it comes, it will eventually pass.

However, while the natural hurricane causes disasters, its causes are simple, its duration is short, and it is still bearable. Only the political and economic hurricanes in historical evolution, although their direction of progress can be foreseen like meteorological events, and there are also methods of resolution and prevention, but the causes are more complex, and the duration is slightly longer, which is not tolerable for the average person. And its harm is more severe than that of a natural hurricane.

The youth of today are like people in a hurricane, under the shock of economic and political turmoil, and due to various reasons such as the inability to see the clearing of the gloom and impatience, some are swallowed up, some escape, some wander, and very few can deal with this hurricane with a calm attitude, like astronomers observing natural hurricanes, and use the results of this observation [to understand] its causes and trends, to seek solutions.

Here, we can say one sentence: There is no education in China today! Written on the night of the storm, September 2, 1933.

Hurricane 245

— Yi Ping

The azure sky connects endlessly with the vast and fertile fields, a gentle breeze lightly blows, the willows hanging over the riverbank wave ripples across the still water. Cuckoos fly across the sky, calling "cuckoo every family," a joyful spirit filling the blue sky and air. The young masters and misses in the city lightly move their noble bodies, and also step into the economically bankrupt countryside, admiring the beauty of nature; however, Ah Xiang, who labors all year round but cannot support his family, at this time, is rolling up his trouser legs, holding a hoe,

[Text obscured, possibly referring to resistance against foreign powers]

loosening the clods of mud in the fields, like an ox; but his ox was sold to the village chief of the east village last year due to the cheap price of grain. He has no good fortune to enjoy this beautiful gift, he must work like an ox. Sowing, transplanting, dividing seedlings, from dawn to sunset. The beautiful blue sky flies away like an arrow in his toiling work. Then comes the summer with the blazing sun in the sky, but the green leaves on the wheat field provide shade, cicadas chirp noisily above, sitting underneath drinking and chatting is also quite pleasant, farmers do not have this blessing! Ah Xiang looks at the inch-long seedlings, wanting to grin; but the heavens have not rained, and every day he hauls water with a pump, the small river running through the east and west villages has become much shallower, and the hundreds of acres of fields in both villages are still absorbing as much as possible, if it doesn't rain for another ten days or half a month, a drought is imminent. Ah Xiang watches the inch-long seedlings, the smile on his lips fades away. A tragedy of selling the ox comes to mind, and two clear tears trickled down his face.

It was a winter morning last year, with snowflakes dancing in the air. His wife shivered in the thin blanket, with no clothes to wear, and no grain was seen in the jar. Ah Xiang was preparing to go to the east village to borrow some rice when a large sedan chair and the village chief came to his door, it was the landlord Master Lu who personally came to the countryside to urge the rent. The farmers in this village are all tenants of Master Lu. Although it was a bumper harvest last year, each dan of grain was only worth five yuan. When paying the rent to the granary, the account was not cleared, and it was agreed that it would be returned to Master Lu by the end of the year; this was the last hope of the villagers, that the few dans of grain could be sold at a good price as a savior. Seeing that the end of the year had arrived, the price of grain was getting cheaper. Ah Xiang's mother had died in the first half of the year, and the costs of the funeral and medical treatment were an immense burden for a poor farmer, so at this time, there was no grain left in his home. Seeing that Master Lu and the village chief had personally come to the countryside, knowing that there was no room for denial, he secretly sold the ox to pay the rent.

This summer, he could only rely on his own two legs to draw water. Fearing that the water in the small river would not be enough to irrigate the hundreds of acres of fields in the two villages, he worked day and night, his feet full of blisters, not daring to rest. Every night he observed the stars, never seeing any sign of rain. Naturally, the farmers in the east and west villages were all frowning. For more than half a year last year, some sold their possessions, some were swindled. If there was another drought this year, the people of the two villages would become refugees. However, it did rain, and the green seedlings were laden with ears of grain. Ah Xiang happily put down a heavy heart.

That night, he was awakened by a loud noise, a terrifying hurricane swept over the roof, the four walls of the house were shaken, and the roof creaked as if it was about to be blown away. Ah Xiang trembled in the torn blanket, not daring to poke his head out, it seemed that many houses nearby had collapsed, with loud cries and shouts. His whole heart was swirling with fear of sacrificing his only dwelling in the storm, his wife was terrified and crying. When the farming tools hanging on the wall fell, they made a loud noise. Whoosh, whoosh, a terrifying hurricane just swept over the roof, the worried couple did not sleep well all night.

But even more frightening things were to follow. The next day, many thatched huts had collapsed nearby. Ah Xiang thought of going to the east village to see his in-laws. Stepping out of the door, the boundless rice fields were lying prostrate in the fields. He felt like he had fallen into an abyss of darkness, his eyes staring at the abundant ears of grain he had reaped with great effort since spring and summer, lying prostrate like a sick man...

Drama

War and Peace (16) (Four-Act Play) 247

— Ling He

Act II: The fleeing crowd

Young Master: There is no such thing, I am the most conscientious person. If you don't believe me, I won't marry a wife in this life to show you.

Auntie: Don't say that, I just don't like to hear these things. The two of us will never be able to stay together for life. Even if I hadn't married your father, you wouldn't be my ideal husband. What's the point? Let's just have fun while we're happy, why talk so far? What's the use of being able to talk but not do?

Young Master: You're starting with that same old routine again, why do you always spoil the mood? Don't you really love me?

Auntie: Why wouldn't I really love you? But I see through everything, let's just do as we go.

(A steam whistle awakens the dreams of this mother and son.)

Young Master: Oh no, the whistle is blowing again, they haven't come yet.

Auntie: I think they should be here now.

Orderly: Young Master! (Enters from the pantry, followed by the station master.) I have now invited the station master, please negotiate with him in person about that matter.

Station Master: Haven't all the family members arrived yet? We have been waiting for a long time. (Looks at his watch.) Originally, this train was supposed to leave at 10:20, but it's already 10:45.

Young Master: I'm sorry, I'm sorry, please sit down.

Station Master: You're welcome. What would you like to discuss, Young Master?

Young Master: It's just a small matter. I'm really sorry to have to ask the station master to come in person. The adjutant in our division said that this carriage was chartered by us, I don't know why there is a female member of another family sitting inside.

Station Master: Did she just arrive?

Young Master: (To the orderly) Did she just arrive?

Orderly: She's been here for a while.

Station Master: Oh! I remember. I originally wanted to come and discuss it with the Young Master in person, but because the refugees were causing trouble, I asked the ticket inspector to bring her. That is Mrs. Wang, the section chief of the provincial government; (in a low voice) she suddenly ran over and asked us for a seat, and I couldn't think of a solution for a while. The first-class seats are all reserved, and she won't sit in second class, and there are no empty seats. So I asked her to squeeze in with you. Because you don't have many family members, and the carriage is large. Please forgive me, Young Master. You know, the section chief's wife, now that she has come, I can't possibly not give her some face. Haha, right?

Young Master: But, Station Master! You have chartered this carriage to me, so you shouldn't... Haha, right?

Station Master: You're right, I shouldn't. But there's really no way, please forgive me, Young Master. ...! There's really nothing to do when you encounter this kind of thing. You see, the outside is full of refugees, all fleeing from the front lines. But there aren't enough trains, and most of them don't have money to buy tickets. They insist on taking the train, is that reasonable?

Young Master: Yes, yes.

Station Master: Everyone wants to take the train, but they don't buy tickets, is that right? If this continues, the government's railway income will disappear. ...

So I have to go and enlighten them now. ... I won't keep you company, Young Master, please sit.

Young Master: Please, please. But that... what should we do?

Auntie: I think we should just let her sit, everyone is just trying to save face.

Station Master: Yes! Really…

Young Master: Thank you, thank you! Thank you, Station Master, for your special help. (Walks out the door, then turns back.) Those people really don't understand reason. Crying and screaming, making a lot of noise, it's simply outrageous, it really makes me angry. It's really difficult to work for the country, I bear the burden and endure the blame! ...Okay, Young Master, goodbye. (Shakes hands and leaves).
